Elections stand as the cornerstone of nation building, representing more than just a procedural event; they symbolize the profound power vested in the citizenry to select their leadership and collectively determine the trajectory of their society. In this democratic framework, the police force serves as the primary guardian of law and order, bearing a fundamental responsibility to cultivate and maintain a peaceful environment throughout the electoral period. The machinery of the police is indispensable in facilitating an electoral process that is transparent, free, and fair, ensuring that every vote is cast without fear, intimidation, or undue influence. Historically, the Election Commission has issued various instructions and operational manuals designed to guide police functioning during these critical times. However, given the evolving complexity of modern elections and the increasingly multifaceted role played by law enforcement agencies, there is a pressing need to consolidate these disparate guidelines into a single, comprehensive handbook. This document is intended to serve as an authoritative guide for the entire police hierarchy, from senior command officers to ground-level personnel, clarifying their specific roles and responsibilities regarding electoral activities.

The handbook encompasses a vast array of topics that require meticulous planning and precise execution by the police force to ensure the integrity of the election. One of the primary components involves the formulation of a district security plan, which acts as a strategic blueprint for deploying resources effectively across a specific geographic area. This planning phase includes the implementation of preventive measures designed to anticipate and neutralize potential threats before they materialize. A critical aspect of this strategy is the concept of vulnerability mapping, a technical process wherein areas prone to electoral malpractice, violence, or coercion are identified and categorized based on risk levels. Closely linked to this is the identification of critical polling stations, which are specific voting locations deemed highly sensitive due to historical precedents of conflict, demographic complexities, or logistical challenges. The handbook also addresses the Model Code of Conduct, often abbreviated as MCC, which is a set of norms established by the Election Commission that political parties and candidates must observe once the election schedule is announced, and it outlines the police duty to enforce these rules impartially. Furthermore, the text details the mechanisms for monitoring election expenditure to prevent the use of illicit funds or bribery, ensuring a level playing field for all contestants.

In addition to local policing strategies, the handbook delineates the role of Central Armed Police Forces, known as CAPFs, which are federal paramilitary units deployed to assist state police in maintaining order, particularly in regions where local resources may be insufficient or where neutrality is paramount. The protection of Very Important Persons, or VIPs, including candidates and high-ranking officials, is another specialized area covered, requiring tailored security protocols to prevent targeted attacks or disruptions. The document also provides special operational plans for areas affected by Left Wing Extremism, referred to as LWE, or other forms of militancy, where the threat landscape involves armed insurgency rather than standard civil unrest. In the digital age, the handbook further expands into social media management, guiding police on how to monitor online platforms for hate speech, fake news, and incitement to violence, which can rapidly escalate into real-world disorder. All these elements culminate in poll day management, the most intense phase of operations, where coordination, rapid response capabilities, and crowd control are essential to ensure that voting proceeds smoothly from opening to closing hours.

To support the human element of this massive logistical undertaking, a comprehensive chapter dedicated to training and welfare measures for police officials has been incorporated into the handbook. This section ensures that the entire police machinery is not only technically proficient but also sensitized to the ethical and legal nuances of the election process. Training modules cover the theoretical concepts of democracy, the practical application of laws, and the behavioral expectations of officers interacting with the public and political actors. Welfare measures are included to maintain high morale and physical readiness among the workforce, recognizing that election duties often involve long hours, high stress, and deployment away from home. To facilitate quick decision-making and easy access to information, the handbook includes practical tools such as checklists for officers at various levels, a collection of frequently asked questions to clarify common doubts, and a compilation of relevant legal provisions that empower police action while safeguarding civil liberties. These resources act as ready references, allowing officers to verify procedures and legal authorities instantly during dynamic situations.

Ultimately, it is expected that this handbook will function as a practical and indispensable guide for all police functionaries involved in the election process. By streamlining activities and providing a unified framework for action, the document aims to equip law enforcement agencies with the necessary tools, strategies, and knowledge to address any issue that may arise within their jurisdiction. The goal is to create a standardized approach to election security that transcends individual interpretation, ensuring consistency and reliability across different regions. Through this structured guidance, the police force can better uphold the sanctity of the democratic process, fostering an environment where the will of the people is expressed freely and safely. The compilation represents a significant step forward in professionalizing election management, bridging the gap between policy intent and ground-level execution, and reinforcing the trust of the populace in the institutions tasked with protecting their democratic rights.

Understanding police organizations and their specific roles and responsibilities during electoral processes is fundamental to the functioning of a healthy democracy. The general mandate of the police force extends far beyond routine law enforcement, particularly when an election is underway. In this critical period, the police are tasked with ensuring the safety and security of the entire polling machinery, which includes all physical infrastructure, personnel, and materials used to conduct the vote. This responsibility begins well before the first ballot is cast and continues until after the final results are declared and all poll materials are securely stored. A primary objective is to provide robust security to candidates, election officials, and the voting public alike. The overarching role of the police during elections is to cultivate a secure, peaceful, and conducive environment where every citizen can exercise their democratic right to vote without any form of interference, coercion, or fear. By upholding the rule of law, the police ensure the legitimacy and integrity of the entire electoral process, thereby reinforcing public trust in democratic institutions.

The duties of the police during elections are multifaceted and require meticulous planning and execution. One of the foremost responsibilities is maintaining law and order in and around polling stations as well as during various events related to election campaigns. This involves preventing voter suppression tactics, which include any attempts at voter intimidation, coercion, or other malicious activities designed to discourage people from participating in the election. The police must ensure that voting takes place in an atmosphere free from the threat of violence or intimidation. Furthermore, they are responsible for providing dedicated security protection to candidates, election officials, and voters who may be at risk. This also extends to securing sensitive election materials and critical infrastructure. The police manage traffic flow to ensure the safe and efficient movement of people traveling to and from polling stations and campaign rallies. A crucial aspect of their duty involves the safe transportation and storage of poll materials, such as ballot papers, Electronic Voting Machines known as EVMs, and Voter Verifiable Paper Audit Trail units referred to as VVPATs. These measures are essential to prevent any possibility of tampering, theft, or destruction of election materials. During political rallies and protests, the police must manage crowds effectively to prevent disturbances, riots, or any untoward incidents that could disrupt the peace. They are also empowered to investigate election-related crimes and take appropriate legal action against perpetrators. This includes enforcing election laws and regulations related to campaign finance, political advertising, and the general conduct of candidates and political parties. The police provide vital assistance to election officials in setting up polling stations and maintaining a secure environment for the counting of votes. They must respond promptly and impartially to any complaints related to the election process. Above all, the police must remain strictly neutral, showing no favoritism towards any political party or candidate. They are bound to uphold the principle of absolute impartiality and neutrality in the discharge of all their official duties, including those related to elections. This includes the strict enforcement of the Model Code of Conduct, a set of guidelines issued by the Election Commission that comes into effect immediately upon the announcement of election dates. Through these actions, the police provide confidence-building measures among the general electorate, assuring them that their votes will be counted fairly and safely.

The role and responsibilities of the Director General of Police, often abbreviated as DGP, who serves as the head of the state police force, are particularly significant in ensuring the success of elections. The DGP is required to establish a specialized Election Cell headed by a duly appointed Special Police Officer or SPNO at least six months prior to the commencement of elections. This cell is designed to streamline all election-related activities and serve as the central command for coordination. The DGP must ensure that this cell is adequately staffed with a sufficient number of Gazetted Officers, who are senior commissioned officers, and other ranks, along with the necessary infrastructural facilities to function effectively. It is the duty of the DGP to ensure that all vacant posts across all districts are filled well in advance, especially those positions critical for election duties. These key positions include Range Inspectors General of Police, Deputy Inspectors General, Commissioners of Police, Senior Superintendents of Police, Superintendents of Police who act as District Police Chiefs, Deputy Superintendents of Police overseeing sub-divisions, and specific DSPs in charge of Assembly Constituencies for election purposes. Additionally, officer-in-charges of police stations and police posts must be appointed without delay. Similarly, the DGP must ensure that crucial election-related posts at the State Headquarters are also filled promptly. The DGP is responsible for ensuring strict compliance with the directions issued by the Election Commission of India regarding the transfer and posting of police officials connected with elections, preventing any last-minute changes that could compromise neutrality.

Furthermore, the DGP must ensure that the Training Division within the police department devises and implements a comprehensive training program for all police officials deputed for election-related duties. This training covers legal aspects, crowd management, conflict resolution, and the specific protocols for handling election materials. The DGP is also accountable for ensuring the timely completion of investigations into all cases related to previous elections, guaranteeing that final reports are filed in the competent courts before the new election cycle begins. This helps clear the backlog of legal issues that could otherwise influence the current electoral atmosphere. The DGP must ensure that the State Protection Review Committee, also known as the Threat Perception Committee, conducts a thorough review of the security arrangements to be provided to all contesting candidates, election-related officials, and other categorized protectees who face threats. Financial preparedness is another critical area; the DGP must ensure that police budget planning for the entire election process, including the funds required for deploying Central Armed Police Forces known as CAPFs, is completed much in advance. The requisite amounts must be disbursed to the districts well in time, and definitely before the arrival of the Central Armed Police Forces in the state, to avoid any logistical bottlenecks. To maintain seamless connectivity, the DGP shall designate an Additional Director General of Police or an Inspector General of Police specifically for Communications. This officer is responsible for procuring, managing, and assessing the requirements for communication systems across the state. They must ensure that reliable wireless communication systems are established at every police station and at all polling locations to facilitate real-time coordination and rapid response.

The strategic oversight of the DGP also extends to national security and internal stability concerns. The DGP must continuously review the activities of terrorists, gangsters, hardened criminals, and individuals or groups propagating left-wing extremism, which refers to insurgent movements often active in rural and forested areas. The DGP must coordinate closely with central security agencies to activate the state police machinery, including the State Intelligence and Counter Intelligence units, to thwart any designs by such elements to disrupt the elections. If the state shares an international border, the DGP must ensure coordination with border protection agencies, including the Central Armed Police Forces deployed there, to secure these sensitive frontiers. Inter-state coordination is equally vital; the DGP must organize meetings with officials of bordering states to ensure complete sealing of inter-state borders and prevent the movement of anti-social elements or illicit materials. Finally, the DGP must ensure the strengthening of interstate and inter-district checkpoints, locally known as nakas, by providing necessary infrastructural facilities and ensuring their round-the-clock operation. These checkpoints serve as critical filters to monitor movement and maintain security throughout the election period, thereby creating a comprehensive security grid that supports the free and fair conduct of democracy.

The comprehensive management of security forces during the conduct of elections involves a multifaceted approach that begins with a rigorous assessment and clear communication regarding the availability and specific requirements of these forces to the chief executive officer of the state, who is typically the Chief Secretary or the head of the state administration. This initial phase is critical as it sets the foundation for the entire security apparatus required to uphold the sanctity of the democratic process. Following this assessment, detailed planning for the deployment of security personnel must be undertaken, a process that heavily relies on referencing and analyzing the deployment plans utilized in previous elections to identify successful strategies and rectify past shortcomings. Concurrently, the responsible authority must obtain formal proposals from various field units regarding the conferment of Executive Magistrate powers upon other designated officers. An Executive Magistrate holds specific legal authorities necessary for maintaining public order, and extending these powers to additional officers ensures a wider net of control and rapid response capability across the election landscape. Ensuring that these powers are officially granted requires active and persistent liaison with the State Home Department, which serves as the administrative backbone for internal security matters within the state. Furthermore, the official must coordinate with the State Home Department to facilitate the issuance of official notifications under section 28-A of the Representation of the People Act, 1951. This specific section of the law provides the legal framework for the deputation of police officers to the Election Commission of India, effectively placing them under the operational control of the election body for the duration of the electoral process to ensure impartiality and focused duty.

A primary objective of this extensive coordination is to mobilize all types of security forces available within the state to guarantee the smooth and uninterrupted conduct of elections. This mobilization is not merely about numbers but involves creating a conducive environment where peace prevails, allowing voters to exercise their franchise without fear or intimidation. To achieve this, elaborate logistical arrangements must be made to support the security forces. These arrangements encompass a wide array of specialized resources including bomb disposal squads equipped to handle explosive threats, mounted police units effective for crowd control in difficult terrains, boats for water-bound constituencies, adequate stocks of ammunition for defense, a fleet of vehicles for rapid mobility, and access to helicopters and air ambulances for emergency medical evacuations or quick deployment to remote areas. The Director General of Police of the state going to polls bears a significant responsibility that extends beyond state borders. They must ensure the movement and mobilization of State Armed Police Forces for deployment in other states as well, strictly adhering to the directions issued by the Ministry of Home Affairs of the Government of India. This inter-state cooperation is vital for balancing security resources across the nation during simultaneous or staggered election phases.

Central to this entire operation is the role and responsibility of the State Police Nodal Officer, a key position appointed in accordance with specific instructions from the Election Commission, notably referenced in instruction number 464/L&O/2023/EPS dated 7th June 2023. This officer acts as the primary link between the police machinery and the election administration, performing a myriad of duties in close coordination with the Chief Electoral Officer. One of the foremost tasks is the preparation of a comprehensive State or Union Territory Force Deployment Plan. This document outlines exactly how security personnel will be positioned and utilized throughout the election period. The plan does not become effective immediately upon drafting; it must undergo a rigorous approval process by a dedicated committee comprising the Chief Electoral Officer, the State Police Nodal Officer, and the State Central Armed Police Forces Nodal Officer. Once this committee approves the draft, it is further vetted and potentially modified by General Observers and Police Observers who are appointed directly by the Election Commission of India to ensure neutrality and adherence to national standards, as detailed in the Manual on Force Deployment published in 2023.

In scenarios where the state faces a deficiency in its police force due to large-scale retirements or a lack of fresh inductions of new recruits, the State Police Nodal Officer must prepare a multilateral augmentation plan. This strategic document outlines the mechanism for borrowing police forces, Home Guards, or other security personnel from neighboring states or union territories based on mutually acceptable terms. This ensures that no state is left vulnerable due to internal staffing shortages. The officer is also tasked with the continuous review and assessment of detailed daily law and order situations within the state or union territory. This involves monitoring real-time data to ensure that timely and effective measures are taken to address specific law and order concerns that may arise in the context of the ongoing elections. Effective coordination with all District Superintendents of Police, Commissioners of Police, and other field officers is essential to disseminate information and enforce election-related protocols uniformly across all jurisdictions. Additionally, the officer must ensure that all police officials deputed for election duties receive specialized training. This is achieved by effecting liaison with the Training Wing of the state police force to organize courses that cover election laws, crowd management, and conflict resolution.

The State Police Nodal Officer is responsible for implementing specific measures for law and order as prescribed by the Election Commission of India. These measures include the rigorous monitoring of past electoral offences to prevent recidivism and the execution of preventive actions to stop potential violations before they occur. A critical component of this strategy is the monitoring of the Vulnerability Mapping process, which involves assessing polling stations that are historically prone to violence, intimidation, or undue influence. Corrective measures must be planned and executed at least six months prior to the elections to neutralize these risks. The officer must also ensure the time-bound execution of non-bailable warrants against individuals involved in electoral crimes, thereby demonstrating the rule of law. Special drives must be launched to unearth and seize illegal arms, ammunition, explosives, drugs, unaccounted cash, illicit liquor, and other contrabands that could be used to disrupt the peace or bribe voters. There must be a strict check on the illegal transportation and storage of cash and other inducements intended to sway the electorate. Any other additional and enhanced measures deemed necessary to maintain and improve the law and order situation must also be proactively adopted.

Reporting mechanisms are equally vital, requiring the preparation and submission of consolidated reports in the LOR-I format, which stands for Law and Order Report, as prescribed by the Election Commission of India. These reports are sent to the State Home Department, where they are consolidated into the LOR-II format. This consolidated data is then submitted to the Chief Electoral Officer of the state for review and subsequently forwarded to the Election Commission of India. This reporting cycle begins from the day the elections are announced and continues until the entire election process is completed, providing a continuous stream of intelligence to the highest authorities. The assessment of the requirement for Central Armed Police Forces, which are federal paramilitary forces deployed from the Government of India, is another crucial duty. The State Police Nodal Officer must convey these requirements to the Chief Electoral Officer through the office of the Director General of Police and the State Home Department, providing proper justification for the numbers requested. Following this, an induction and de-induction plan for these Central Armed Police Forces must be prepared in consultation with the State Level Force Coordinator of the Ministry of Home Affairs, ensuring that forces arrive and depart in an organized manner without creating security vacuums.

Logistical support for the Central Armed Police Forces is a massive undertaking that requires a detailed plan for accommodation, transportation, and the management of food and rations. This plan must account for the security of these forces whether they are on the move between locations or stationed on static duty at sensitive points. A phase-wise movement plan for all forces must be prepared and constantly monitored to ensure that troops reach their designated posts exactly when needed, as outlined in the 2023 Manual on Force Deployment. Contingency planning is also mandatory, covering scenarios that require rescue operations, evacuation of injured personnel, hospitalization, air transportation, and water transportation. This involves coordinating with various government departments and agencies to ensure seamless integration of services during emergencies. The officer must create a comprehensive database of all helipads and airfields within the jurisdiction and deploy a system for inbound and outbound frisking to prevent the smuggling of weapons or contraband via air routes. Close coordination with the police setups of bordering states is required for inter-state border sealing and joint operations to prevent criminals from fleeing across jurisdictional lines. Furthermore, coordination with officials of the Central Armed Police Forces manning the international border and other border agencies is essential to ensure the sealing of international borders, if any exist in the region, at least 72 hours before polling begins to stop cross-border interference.

Finally, the implementation of a robust communication plan prepared by the Additional Director General of Police or Inspector General of Police in charge of wireless communications is imperative. This plan must ensure a proper and reliable communication system even in shadow zones, which are areas where standard radio signals might be blocked by terrain or structures. Without reliable communication, command and control during an election can collapse, leading to chaotic responses to incidents. The State Police Nodal Officer must also prepare detailed security plans for critical infrastructure such as dispatch centers where materials are sent out, receiving centers where they arrive, training centers where personnel are briefed, strong rooms where electronic voting machines and ballots are stored, and warehouses holding election supplies. Every aspect of these facilities must be secured against sabotage, theft, or unauthorized access, ensuring that the physical integrity of the election material is maintained from the moment it is printed or manufactured until it is counted after the polls close. Through these exhaustive measures, the state machinery works to guarantee that the election is conducted in a free, fair, and peaceful manner, upholding the democratic rights of every citizen.

The comprehensive framework for maintaining security during elections in regions affected by left wing extremism, active insurgency, or those situated along international borders begins with the formulation of a specialized security plan tailored to the unique threats of each area. This planning process is not generic but requires a deep understanding of local geopolitical dynamics and historical patterns of violence. A critical component of this strategy involves establishing regular and close coordination with police observers who act as the eyes and ears of the election commission on the ground, ensuring that real-time intelligence flows seamlessly between field operatives and command centers. Security planners must meticulously identify routes within the state that are prone to improvised explosive devices, commonly known as IEDs, which are homemade bombs constructed from non-military components and often used by insurgent groups to target security forces and disrupt democratic processes. Once these dangerous corridors are mapped, the information must be immediately circulated to the Central Armed Police Forces, a collective term for various federal paramilitary organizations deployed to assist state police in maintaining order. This circulation of intelligence is vital for both left wing extremism hotspots and areas suffering from militancy or insurgency. Furthermore, advance planning is essential for the smooth induction and de-induction of these central forces, requiring the preparation of detailed route charts that account for terrain, potential ambush points, and logistical stopovers. To manage the complex movement and deployment of multiple units from different central armed police forces arriving in the state simultaneously, a dedicated State Control Room must be established. This hub serves as the nerve center for coordinating operations, ensuring that the vast manpower of the central forces is utilized optimally not just for security but also for confidence-building measures among the local populace who may be fearful due to past violence. Before deployment, all incoming forces must be provided with comprehensive checklists, clear guidelines on dos and don'ts, election-specific booklets, and other relevant materials to ensure they understand their mandate. Coordination with the Chief Electoral Officer is paramount to align security deployments with electoral timelines and requirements, ensuring that the presence of force enhances rather than hinders the voting process. The District Police Chief, whether holding the title of Commissioner of Police, Senior Superintendent of Police, or Superintendent of Police depending on the administrative structure of the district, bears the ultimate responsibility for reviewing election preparedness regularly and adapting strategies as the situation evolves.

At the district level, the senior police leadership is tasked with translating the broad state-level security plan into a granular district deployment plan that contains micro-details specific to local conditions and requirements. This localized plan must address the unique challenges of each village, town, and polling station within the district boundaries. It is imperative that there is absolutely no deviation from either the state or district deployment plans without obtaining express prior approval from the most senior General or Police Observer present, as unauthorized changes can create security gaps that adversaries might exploit. The complete and faithful implementation of the district deployment plan is non-negotiable and forms the backbone of election security. A significant aspect of this role involves assessing the precise need for central armed police forces based on the deployment patterns established at the state headquarters and arranging for all necessary logistical support, including food, shelter, and transport, to ensure the forces can operate effectively. Before commencing duties, the jawans, a term referring to the constabulary or enlisted personnel of the central armed police forces, must be thoroughly briefed by senior officers regarding the guidelines issued by the Honorable Election Commission of India and the relevant legal provisions governing elections. To facilitate this, organized training workshops should be conducted to ensure every member of the force understands the legal boundaries of their authority and the specific protocols for election duty. Financial welfare is also a key consideration; the honorarium or special allowance payable to these personnel must be verified and certified well in advance to ensure it is disbursed without any delay, strictly adhering to the rules and instructions issued by the Election Commission. Furthermore, security commanders must ensure that no central armed police force unit is kept idle in reserve; instead, the entire contingent must be deployed on active election duty as stipulated by the guidelines, maximizing the security footprint. Specific strength requirements dictate that in normal areas, central armed police forces must not be deployed in less than half-section strength at critical polling booths, while in areas affected by left wing extremism or general disturbance, the minimum strength at such critical locations must not be less than one full section, reflecting the higher threat levels in these zones. After the conclusion of duties, a formal de-briefing session must be held with the officers and personnel of the central armed police forces to gather feedback and lessons learned. Additionally, the district administration is responsible for providing vehicles and adequate reserves of POL, an acronym for petrol, oil, and lubricants, to facilitate the movement of these forces to their next destination, headquarters, or another state where elections are scheduled.

The communication infrastructure during elections is as critical as the physical deployment of troops, requiring the strict implementation of a communication plan prepared by the Additional Director General of Police or Inspector General of Police in charge of wireless communications. This plan must guarantee a robust communication system that covers even shadow zones, which are geographical areas where standard radio signals are blocked by mountains, dense forests, or urban structures, potentially leaving security teams isolated. To ensure the smooth conduct of the electoral process, police communication networks including wireless radio sets, Polnet which is a dedicated police data network, and local or wide area networks known as LAN and WAN must be utilized extensively. Wireless sets, which are portable two-way radios, should be provided at every sensitive polling station and carried in the escort vehicles of election observers, Sub Divisional Magistrates who oversee clusters of polling stations, every route zone or sector patrolling party, and by the officers commanding central armed police force units. Furthermore, vehicles belonging to senior supervisory officers must be fitted with wireless sets, and indeed all official vehicles involved in election duty should possess this capability to maintain constant connectivity. These wireless communication networks must remain operational continuously until the polling process is fully concluded and all polling materials, including the sensitive Electronic Voting Machines or EVMs which record votes digitally, are securely transported back to the strong room, a highly secured vault for storing election equipment. In addition to wireless systems, communication between different agencies should be established through static landlines and mobile phones available with concerned officers to create redundant channels of contact. To further facilitate smooth communication, SIM cards or recharge vouchers should be provided to key supervisory officers of the security forces deployed on election duty, ensuring they have uninterrupted mobile connectivity. A comprehensive list containing the mobile phone numbers of all in-charge officers of sector patrolling parties and senior supervisory police officers operating within their respective districts, including relevant officials from the central armed police forces and state armed police, must be maintained. This vital contact information should be kept readily available at all District Police Election Cells, District Police Control Rooms, and the State Police Control Room to enable rapid coordination during emergencies.

Finally, the management of firearms and ammunition is governed by strict compliance with instructions issued by the Election Commission, specifically referencing the measures related to law and order for conducting peaceful, free, and fair general or bye-elections as dated June 8, 2023. This involves a rigorous order checking process for all arms licenses held by civilians within the district to prevent the misuse of legally owned weapons during the volatile election period. Based on this verification, the police leadership must recommend cases for the temporary suspension of arms licenses to the District Magistrate, who also serves as the District Electoral Officer, thereby reducing the overall volume of circulating firearms and minimizing the risk of violence or intimidation at the polls. This systematic approach to disarmament, combined with the detailed deployment, logistical, and communication strategies outlined above, creates a multi-layered security apparatus designed to protect the sanctity of the democratic process even in the most challenging and hostile environments. The integration of central and state forces, underpinned by clear chains of command, advanced planning, and seamless communication, ensures that every voter can cast their ballot without fear, regardless of whether they reside in a tranquil urban center or a conflict-ridden border region.

To guarantee that every individual holding a license for firearms is properly notified regarding the mandatory deposition of their weapons during sensitive periods, the relevant details concerning these licensed arms must be readily accessible through the centralized digital repository known as the National Database of Arms Licenses, commonly referred to by its acronym NDALALIS. This online system serves as the primary source of truth for verifying ownership and status of legal firearms across the jurisdiction. The District Magistrate, who acts as the chief executive officer of the district administration, bears the critical responsibility of ensuring that the local databases under their supervision are kept continuously up to date with the latest information. Furthermore, the District Magistrate must facilitate the seamless sharing of this data with the corresponding District Police Authorities to ensure full compliance with the strict directives issued by the Election Commission of India, the constitutional body responsible for administering free and fair elections in the country. Immediately following the official announcement of an election schedule, a comprehensive review process must be initiated involving the physical verification of all arms held by licensees within the district boundaries. This phase marks the beginning of stringent regulatory measures, which include the compulsory depositing of all licensed firearms at designated police stations and a complete moratorium on the issuance of any new arms licenses. These actions are taken strictly in accordance with the standing orders and directions promulgated by the Election Commission of India to prevent the misuse of weapons during the electoral process.

The administration must ensure one hundred percent scrutiny of every existing arms license alongside a thorough inventory audit of all licensed arm shops to account for every weapon and ammunition round in circulation. Concurrently, law enforcement agencies are mandated to carry out aggressive operations for the seizure of illegal arms, unauthorized ammunition, explosives, illicit drugs, and unaccounted cash that may be used to influence voters or fund unlawful activities. A regime of strict vigilance and meticulous checking of vehicles must be established at key entry and exit points to ensure that no undesirable elements, criminals, or concealed weapons including ammunition are being transported into the state from outside jurisdictions. Intelligence gathering mechanisms must be activated to collect specific information regarding the illegal manufacture, clandestine transport, and distribution networks of arms, ammunition, and liquor, followed by immediate and effective legal action against those involved. A special nationwide or state-wide drive must be launched targeting proclaimed offenders, individuals who have absconded from justice, bail jumpers who have violated court conditions, and those against whom Non-Bailable Warrants have been issued, as well as identified drug smugglers. During the actual days of polling and the immediate run-up to the election, actions against smugglers and suppliers of narcotics must be further intensified to maintain public order. A policy of zero tolerance must be adopted and strictly enforced towards the smuggling, supply, and distribution of drugs amongst the general population and specifically among voters in the period leading up to the polling day, as substance abuse can be utilized to compromise the integrity of the voting process.

To effectively curb the flow of illicit substances, there must be a significant strengthening of police checkpoints, locally known as nakas, situated at inter-state borders, inter-district boundaries, and international frontiers where applicable. A specialized operational drive should be initiated by the State Police within a window of one hundred and twenty days prior to the date of completion of the term of the parliamentary or legislative assembly. The objective of this drive is to update and verify the master list of all proclaimed offenders, absconders, and parole jumpers to ensure they are monitored or apprehended before the election model code of conduct comes into force. Legal cases involving the forfeiture of properties that have been illegally acquired by smugglers and criminal elements must be expedited through the judicial process. Necessary liaison and coordination must be effected with the Competent Authority within the Government of India to fast-track these asset recovery proceedings, thereby dismantling the economic power of criminal syndicates. To achieve these multifaceted security goals, regular district-level coordination meetings must be ensured involving a wide array of stakeholders. These participants must include the Commissioners of Police, Senior Superintendents of Police, and Superintendents of Police from the host district as well as from adjacent districts of neighboring states if the geography warrants it. The intelligence apparatus of both the state government and the Central Government must be integrated into these meetings to elicit actionable intelligence that can prevent crimes before they occur.

The coordination framework must also include the District Magistrate who simultaneously serves as the District Election Officer, along with other district-level election functionaries responsible for logistical planning. Local State Excise authorities must be present to address issues related to illegal liquor which often fuels election violence, while local Income Tax authorities should contribute financial intelligence to track unexplained expenditures by candidates or criminal groups. Municipal authorities must be tasked with checking and removing illegal hoardings and banners that violate election spending limits or public space regulations. Representatives from the Narcotic Control Bureau, an agency under the Ministry of Home Affairs of the Government of India, must be included to coordinate specific actions against high-level drug smugglers operating across borders. Local officers from the Directorate of Intelligence under the Ministry of Finance, Government of India, should attend to provide insights into financial crimes and money laundering linked to election funding. Where applicable, local Customs and Central Excise Authorities must join to monitor the movement of taxed and restricted goods. State Health authorities and the Chief Drug Controller of the State are essential members to regulate pharmaceutical drugs that could be misused. Additionally, officers from the Central Armed Police Forces, which are federal paramilitary units deployed to assist state police in maintaining order, must be part of these strategic discussions to align deployment strategies.

A critical component of the security architecture involves the complete sealing of international borders, state boundaries, and district lines to create a secure perimeter around the election zone. In cases where international borders exist, complete sealing must be executed through effective liaison with the Central Armed Police Forces who are permanently stationed to guard these frontiers, as well as other specialized security agencies. Strong police checkpoints or nakas must be deployed at strategic locations, and the police personnel detailed to these posts must be equipped with modern technology such as Electronic Challan Point of Sale devices. These devices allow for the instant issuance of fines and records. Furthermore, officers must have easy and real-time access to the online Crime and Criminal Tracking Network and Systems, known as CCTNS, which enables the instant verification of the identity of persons and the registration details of vehicles under scrutiny. This integration of human resources with modern technology ensures optimal usage of available forces. These smart nakas, established at inter-state and inter-district entry and exit points, must be fitted with Closed-Circuit Television cameras that capture the entire procedure of checking and verification for the purpose of record-keeping, evidence collection, and subsequent review by supervisory officers. Provisions can and should be made for establishing a one-stop Smart Naka model manned by representatives from various enforcement agencies such as the Excise Department, the Transport Department, and the Anti-Narcotics Task Force unit. This multi-agency approach allows for early intervention and prompt action against diverse types of violations without causing unnecessary delays to legitimate travelers. It is imperative to ensure that all roads originating from or leading to the border areas are effectively covered with adequate deployment of security forces to prevent bypassing of main checkpoints. Additionally, a secondary layer of defense must be created by installing CCTV camera surveillance systems at all nakas positioned at the second line of defence all along the international border to monitor any breaches that might occur at the primary line.

Providing robust security to election functionaries, candidates, and independent observers is a paramount duty that requires precise planning and execution. Security protection for candidates and election observers will be provided by the Commissioner of Police, Senior Superintendent of Police, or Superintendent of Police, depending on the rank appropriate for the district, immediately after the filing of nomination papers by the candidates. This provision of security must be based on a professional assessment of the threat level perceived by the individual and should not be granted in a routine or automatic manner without justification. It must be strictly ensured that all Personal Security Officers, often abbreviated as PSOs, who are deployed to protect candidates, are physically fit and in sound health capable of handling demanding security duties. If any Personal Security Officer proceeds on leave or falls sick during the critical election period, a substitute officer must be provided immediately to fill the gap. Under no circumstances should a candidate or observer be left without security coverage at any point in time, including during night hours when vulnerability may increase. The senior police leadership, specifically the Commissioner of Police, Senior Superintendent of Police, or Superintendent of Police, shall ensure that proper scaled ammunition, meaning the correct type and quantity of bullets authorized for their weapons, is provided to the PSOs and gunmen assigned to the candidate or observer. To oversee this complex arrangement, an officer of the rank of Deputy Superintendent of Police must be appointed as the nodal officer responsible for the deployment, rotation, and checking of security provided to the candidates and observers. There should not be any scope for complacency or laxity on this issue given the high stakes of electoral democracy. Furthermore, the Deputy Superintendent of Police in charge of the Police Lines, along with the Reserve Inspector or Police Lines Officer of the District, should be deputed to take care of the welfare needs of these Personal Security Officers. This includes ensuring they have access to adequate food, clean water, rest facilities, and other logistical support required to maintain their alertness and effectiveness throughout the duration of their protective assignment.

The maintenance of public order and the assurance of security during electoral processes, particularly involving high-profile political figures known as star campaigners, require a meticulously orchestrated series of protective measures. These individuals, due to their prominence and influence, often attract large gatherings that can quickly become unmanageable without proper regulation. Therefore, it is imperative for law enforcement agencies to establish robust crowd control mechanisms that not only facilitate the smooth movement of these dignitaries but also prevent any potential breaches of peace. This responsibility extends to the protection of Election Observers, who play a critical role in ensuring the fairness and transparency of the electoral process. These observers must be provided with adequate security details to shield them from any form of intimidation or harm, thereby allowing them to perform their duties without fear or favor. Furthermore, a comprehensive and forward-looking security plan must be devised well in advance for those protectees who have been categorized as threatened based on credible intelligence inputs. The primary objective of such planning is to guarantee that every visit by a threatened dignitary within a specific jurisdiction concludes peacefully, without any incidents of violence or disruption. To achieve this, there must be a sufficient deployment of police personnel at all election-related events, including rallies, street meetings, and road shows. The presence of a visible and capable police force acts as a deterrent against various forms of criminal activity that could derail the democratic process. Specifically, authorities must ensure that there is absolutely no opportunity for kidnapping or abduction of contesting candidates or their election agents. Additionally, stringent measures must be taken to prevent terrorist activities such as targeted killings, improvised explosive device explosions, and bomb blasts, as well as mass killings and communal, caste, or sectarian riots that could erupt during the heightened tensions of an election period.

A fundamental component of this overarching security strategy involves the systematic mapping of vulnerabilities and the identification of polling stations deemed critical due to their susceptibility to unrest or malpractice. This exercise is of paramount importance and must be initiated significantly early, ideally six to four months prior to the anticipated date of the elections. Such early initiation allows the state machinery to accurately project the requirements for Central Armed Police Forces, which are specialized federal units deployed to assist state police in maintaining order. By starting this process well in advance, logistical challenges can be addressed, and resources can be allocated efficiently. However, to prevent the unnecessary inflation of resource requests, it is essential that the rationale for labeling any specific polling station as critical or normal is documented with clarity and precision. Vulnerable polling stations are inherently categorized as critical, and the justification for this classification must be explicitly stated and subsequently approved by both the Superintendent of Police and the District Collector, who serves as the district's top administrative officer. Although the projected numbers may not be absolute, they serve as a crucial baseline for planning and fund allocation. The task of vulnerability mapping and identifying critical locations must be executed in close coordination with the civilian sector incharge, ensuring a unified approach between civil administration and law enforcement. To facilitate this collaboration, a Deputy Superintendent of Police, who oversees a sub-division, should be formally deputed to maintain liaison with the Sub-Divisional Magistrate of the respective area. Similarly, at a more granular level, a sector police officer should be paired with a civilian sector officer to conduct these mapping exercises on the ground. This collaborative framework, as outlined in the Manual on Vulnerability Mapping from 2023, ensures that all stakeholders are aligned in their understanding of the risks and the necessary countermeasures.

Following the identification phase, several specific actions must be undertaken to secure the electoral process at these critical junctures. The first step involves formally identifying these critical polling stations in close consultation with the District Magistrate, who also functions as the District Election Officer, along with other key election functionaries. Once identified, a range of protective measures must be implemented at these locations to safeguard the integrity of the voting process. This includes ensuring the proper deployment of security forces, with a significant emphasis on the presence of Central Armed Police Forces. It is mandatory that all critical polling stations are guarded by these federal forces, supplemented by non-CAPF measures such as webcasting, which allows for real-time video streaming of the polling process, and the deployment of micro-observers who monitor proceedings at a very localized level. Videography and photography are also employed to create an immutable record of events, acting as both a deterrent to malpractice and evidence for any subsequent inquiries. The compiled list of all such critical polling stations must be shared with the Commanding and Assistant Commanding Officers of the Central Armed Police Forces, enabling them to maintain a constant watch over these sensitive locations. Furthermore, the polling parties, which are the teams responsible for conducting the election at each booth, must be thoroughly briefed about the vulnerable areas and the specific locations of critical polling stations so they can remain vigilant and prepared for any contingency.

Beyond the polling stations themselves, the security of storage centers and counting centers where electronic voting machines and other election materials are kept is equally vital. These facilities, often referred to as strong rooms, serve as the vaults for the democratic instruments of the nation and must be protected with the highest degree of diligence. Effective liaison with the District Magistrate-cum-District Election Officer is essential to formulate and execute a comprehensive security plan for these premises. A two-tier security cordon system must be established around strong rooms, wherein the inner perimeter is secured by the Central Armed Police Forces, providing a core layer of defense, while the outer perimeter is manned by the State Armed Police, creating a secondary buffer zone. For counting centers, which become active after the polling concludes, a more rigorous three-tier security cordon is required. In this arrangement, the first and innermost cordon is maintained by the Central Armed Police Forces, the second cordon by the State Armed Police, and the third and outermost cordon by the regular State Police. This layered approach ensures that any attempt to breach the facility would have to overcome multiple lines of defense. Additionally, appropriate and robust barricading must be installed around the strong rooms to physically impede unauthorized access. The structural integrity of the strong room itself must be assessed to ensure it is in a safe condition from a security perspective. A thorough physical inspection and an anti-sabotage check of the entire premises, including the strong room interior, must be conducted to rule out the presence of any explosive devices or tampering.

Reliability of infrastructure within these secure facilities is another critical aspect that demands attention. An uninterrupted two-way power supply must be guaranteed for the buildings housing the electronic voting machines to prevent any data loss or operational failure. To mitigate the risk of power outages, a standby electricity generator equipped with an automatic turn-on system should be installed within the campus of the building containing the strong room. This ensures that in the event of a main power failure, the backup system kicks in immediately without manual intervention. To manage these technical systems effectively, technically trained personnel should be stationed near the campus in three rotating shifts, ensuring twenty-four-hour coverage. Adequate lighting arrangements must be made throughout the entire premises to eliminate dark spots that could be exploited by intruders. The boundary wall of the campus must be inspected regularly to ensure it is not damaged or compromised in any way, serving as a solid physical barrier. All entry and exit gates of the campus must be continuously manned by security personnel to control access strictly. Communication is the lifeline of any security operation; therefore, a proper communication system, including wireless sets, must be installed across the campus. A comprehensive communication plan should be drafted to coordinate responses during emergencies, and sentries along with their incharges should be equipped with walkie-talkie sets for instant connectivity.

Fire safety is yet another dimension of security that cannot be overlooked in the context of storing sensitive election material. Foolproof fire-fighting arrangements must be established at these locations to prevent any catastrophic loss due to accidental or deliberate fires. This includes positioning both large and small fire tenders, as well as portable fire extinguishers, strategically within the campus of the building. Regular inspections of the entire premises must be carried out by senior officers to verify that all safety protocols are being followed. During these inspections, particular attention should be paid to the condition of the building structure, electrical fittings, sanitary fittings, and water supply systems to ensure they are functioning correctly. Special care must be taken to eliminate any possibility of fire caused by short circuits in the electrical wiring during the storage period, as such an incident could destroy the voting machines and compromise the entire election outcome in that constituency. By adhering to these detailed and multi-layered security protocols, the election machinery can ensure that the democratic process remains free, fair, and secure from any internal or external threats.

Officers who are designated as being in charge of specific jurisdictions or operational units shall be formally instructed to carry out a comprehensive and detailed survey of all electrical wiring systems within their assigned areas. This process involves a physical inspection of the infrastructure to identify any frayed wires, overloaded circuits, unauthorized connections, or outdated installations that could pose a fire hazard or risk of electrocution. Upon completion of this rigorous examination, these officers must furnish an official certificate of fitness, which serves as a formal declaration that the electrical systems meet safety standards and are fit for continued use. In parallel with these electrical safety measures, the local Municipal Authorities are tasked with a critical responsibility to inspect all water supply pipelines and sewage manholes throughout the campus or designated zone. The objective of this inspection is to proactively prevent flooding incidents that could arise from leaked pipes, blocked drainage channels, or structural failures in the sewage system. Such flooding could not only damage property but also disrupt essential services and create unsanitary conditions, so preemptive checking is vital to ensure the integrity of the water and waste management infrastructure.

The duties assigned to senior police leadership, specifically the Commissioner of Police, Senior Superintendent of Police, or Superintendent of Police depending on the administrative structure of the region, encompass a wide range of law enforcement and preventive actions. A primary responsibility is to ensure the effective implementation of prohibitory orders issued by the competent authority under Section 144 of the Code of Criminal Procedure. This legal provision empowers authorities to restrict certain activities in anticipation of potential unrest, and in this context, it is especially focused on banning the carrying of licensed arms in public spaces to reduce the likelihood of violence. Furthermore, these senior officers must ensure that effective preventive actions are taken under relevant sections of the law, such as Sections 107 and 110 of the Code of Criminal Procedure. These sections allow magistrates to demand security from individuals who are likely to commit breaches of peace or have habitual criminal tendencies, thereby acting as a legal deterrent against identified sources of trouble before any crime occurs. They are also responsible for enforcing laws related to the protection of public and private property against defacement, such as graffiti or vandalism, and for regulating the use of loudspeakers to prevent noise pollution and the incitement of communal tensions through amplified sound.

To maintain public order, these senior leaders must organize regular and intensive patrolling operations in high-traffic public places. These locations include bus stands, railway stations, hotels, lodges, and weekly markets, which are often crowded and can become targets for criminal activity or sites of public disorder. During election periods, this patrolling becomes even more critical, as officers must conduct intensive checks throughout the entire area to detect and prevent electoral malpractices such as booth capturing, voter intimidation, or the distribution of illicit money. As part of this effort, they are required to compile a comprehensive list of persons who were involved in electoral offenses during past elections and track the legal disposal or status of their cases. Additionally, they must continuously update lists of known criminals, including history sheeters who have a record of repeated offenses, hardened criminals, musclemen hired for muscle power, militants, declared absconders who are hiding from the law, and fugitives. This updating process includes verifying if any of these individuals hold arms licenses and ensuring that license cancellation actions are taken in accordance with the law and directions issued by the Election Commission of India.

Another crucial administrative duty involves giving effect to the service of pending warrants and challans, which are legal documents summoning individuals to court or citing them for offenses, and maintaining an up-to-date list of those that remain unexecuted. Senior officers must also expedite the investigation and prosecution of any pending electoral offenses to ensure that justice is delivered swiftly and that offenders do not evade accountability due to procedural delays. In the realm of substance control, they are tasked with unearthing illicit liquor factories and distillation centers that operate outside the legal framework, as the flow of illegal alcohol often fuels violence and corruption during sensitive periods like elections. This requires regular reporting on preventive actions taken, seizures of cash and liquor made, and a thorough review of these operations to implement corrective measures where necessary. Furthermore, they must ensure that daily law and order reports for the district are prepared in the prescribed format and transmitted promptly to the State Police Nodal Officer. This officer then compiles the data from various districts and submits it to the State Home Department, creating a centralized view of the security situation. Finally, they are responsible for monitoring election-related expenditure by political candidates and parties to ensure compliance with the financial guidelines set forth by the Election Commission of India, preventing the use of black money in the electoral process.

At the sub-divisional level, the Deputy Superintendent of Police or the officer in charge of a sub-division has specific compliance obligations to ensure the smooth functioning of the justice and security apparatus. They must ensure that all investigations into criminal cases that were registered during previous elections within their area of jurisdiction are brought to completion. This includes ensuring that the chargesheet, which is the final police report detailing the evidence and accusations, or the final closure report, is submitted to the competent judicial authorities without delay. They are also responsible for ensuring that all Non-Bailable Warrants, which are court orders for the arrest of individuals accused of serious crimes where bail is not a right, are executed effectively. To support this, Station House Officers, who are the heads of individual police stations, must compile lists of proclaimed offenders, absconders, and parole jumpers. Based on these lists, lookout circulars must be issued to alert other law enforcement agencies, and concerted efforts must be made to locate and arrest these individuals. The Sub Divisional officer must also verify that lists of potential troublemakers, goonda elements known for violent behavior, hardened criminals, and persons who indulged in crime during the last elections have been accurately compiled by the Station House Officers. Coordination is key, so they must ensure regular meetings are held with adjacent sub-divisions and districts to share important intelligence and synchronize their strategies. Above all, they must ensure meticulous compliance with all directions issued by higher authorities regarding elections, particularly the binding guidelines issued by the Election Commission of India.

The Officer-in-Charge of a police station, commonly known as the Station House Officer or SHO, bears the direct operational responsibility for maintaining law and order at the grassroots level. They must ensure that all pending investigations regarding criminal cases registered during previous elections are completed diligently. Regarding arrests, they must execute non-bailable warrants immediately and ensure that no such warrant remains pending for execution for more than ten days, thereby demonstrating efficiency and adherence to judicial timelines. The SHO is required to compile a list of all proclaimed offenders and absconders pertaining to their specific police station and take necessary legal action to apprehend them. Preventive action is a major component of their role, requiring them to initiate measures that maintain peace during the election period. This involves analyzing patterns of crime, with special attention to the recent and past history of agitations and skirmishes between supporters of various political parties. By identifying these patterns and listing potential troublemakers, the SHO can initiate suitable preventive actions, such as rounding up suspects or increasing surveillance, before violence erupts. They must also share information regarding inter-district illegal activities to prevent criminals from exploiting jurisdictional boundaries.

Security provision is another vital duty of the Station House Officer. They must regularly check and ensure the security of candidates participating in elections, as well as the safety of political rallies, road shows, and corner meetings where politicians interact with voters. They are specifically tasked with ensuring the security of threatened dignitaries or categorized protectees who visit their jurisdiction for election campaigns, as these individuals may be targets of assassination or attack. The SHO must also ensure that patrolling and regular checking of transient accommodations such as hotels, sarais, and dharamshalas are conducted frequently, as these are places where criminals and antisocial elements generally stay to evade detection. Furthermore, they must ensure the security of election observers and election officers who visit their area to monitor the fairness of the process. In the event of a crime, especially those related to elections, the SHO must immediately visit the scene of the incident to oversee the initial investigation and evidence collection. To control movement across boundaries, they must ensure the functioning of nakas, which are temporary police checkpoints established at inter-district and inter-state links. These checkpoints must operate round the clock, and sufficient numbers of police force must be deployed to cover all roads, link roads, and kutcha tracks, which are unpaved rural paths, that connect different states or districts. Intensive checking of vehicles passing through these naka points should be carried out during this sensitive period to intercept illegal weapons, cash, or liquor. It is also mandatory to check that the Closed Circuit Television surveillance systems installed at these checkpoints are functional twenty-four hours a day to provide visual records of all movements. Finally, the SHO must identify pockets of areas that are infested with crime or drug peddling and provide round-the-clock police patrolling or establish fixed police picketing in these zones to deter criminal activity.

The overarching framework for managing security resources is defined by the State and District Security Deployment Plan. The State Deployment Plan is a strategic document that factors in the specific requirements of different districts based on the District Deployment Plans prepared by each district administration. The preparation of a District Deployment Plan is a critical exercise that requires a thorough assessment of available resources. This planning process takes into account the police forces being made available by the State Government to the district, which forms the core local response capability. It also integrates the Central Armed Police Forces, which are federal paramilitary units deployed to assist state police during times of heightened security needs such as elections. Additionally, the plan considers other forces being made available from the State pool, which may include specialized units or reserve forces, as well as the forces already permanently stationed within the district. By synthesizing these various sources of manpower and equipment, the deployment plan ensures that resources are allocated efficiently to areas of highest risk, ensuring comprehensive coverage and the ability to respond rapidly to any emerging threats across the entire region. This hierarchical planning approach ensures that every level of command, from the state headquarters down to the individual police checkpoint, operates with a clear understanding of their roles, resources, and objectives in maintaining public order and ensuring free and fair elections.

At the state level, the comprehensive security and operational plan for elections is meticulously prepared by the State Police Nodal Officer or the State Force Coordinator. This preparation is conducted separately for areas affected by Left Wing Extremism and for those constituencies that are not affected by such extremism, ensuring that the unique challenges of each region are addressed with tailored strategies. This critical planning phase is executed in close consultation with the Chief Electoral Officer, who provides overarching guidance to align security measures with electoral integrity standards. The resulting State Plan serves as a master compilation that aggregates and synthesizes the individual District Plans submitted from across the state. This overarching document explicitly enumerates the specific roles and duties of every officer involved in the election process, creating a clear chain of command and responsibility. Furthermore, the plan includes a thorough assessment of the various resources required, such as the number of security forces needed, logistical support requirements, communication equipment inventories, and specialized security gear. It also contains a detailed training schedule for all forces, mandating pre-induction training to ensure every personnel member is adequately prepared before deployment. The plan addresses complex logistical needs, including the formal requisition of helicopters, air ambulances, and satellite phones to ensure mobility and connectivity in remote or difficult terrains. A strategic component of the plan focuses on communication shadow zones, which are areas where standard mobile networks fail to function, requiring alternative communication strategies and regular coordination meetings with the Telecom Department, Bharat Sanchar Nigam Limited, and other Telecommunication Service Providers to guarantee uninterrupted connectivity during the electoral period.

The District Deployment Plan, which forms the foundational layer of the state strategy, is formulated and finalized through a collaborative effort between the District Magistrate or District Election Officer and the Superintendent of Police or Commissioner of Police responsible for that jurisdiction. Upon the arrival of an Observer appointed by the Election Commission of India to the district, a formal briefing is conducted jointly by the District Magistrate and the senior police leadership, which may include the Senior Superintendent of Police, Superintendent of Police, or Commissioner of Police. During this briefing, the views and recommendations of the Observer are actively sought and must be given serious consideration in finalizing the deployment strategy. Both the State Deployment Plan and the District Deployment Plan are required to be finalized well in advance of the actual polling day to allow sufficient time for resource mobilization and troop movement. These plans are designed to ensure the full and optimal utilization of Central Armed Police Forces and State Armed Police forces, maximizing their effectiveness while minimizing waste. The District Deployment Plan is specifically prepared jointly by the District Election Officer and the Superintendent of Police and must subsequently be vetted by the Senior Most General and Police Observers working together to ensure compliance with national standards. This local deployment plan is derived from the broader state plan but contains micro-level detailing that is strictly based on the specific local situation and immediate requirements of the district.

Strict adherence to the approved plans is mandatory, and it is ensured that there is no deviation from the established protocols without the express prior approval of the Senior Most General or the Police Observer. Specific guidelines govern the minimum strength of forces deployed at critical polling booths. In normal areas, Central Armed Police Forces must not be deployed in strengths less than half a section, which is a standard military unit size, whereas in areas affected by Naxalite insurgency or other disturbances, the minimum strength at critical polling booths must not be less than one full section to provide robust security against potential threats. The plan must also include a sketch map for each sector within the district, clearly identifying vulnerable pockets and critical polling stations that require heightened attention. Security cover for contesting candidates is provided strictly based on a formal assessment of the threat level they face and is not granted as a routine entitlement to all candidates. To protect the integrity of the vote counting process, a three-tier cordoning system is established around counting centers to prevent unauthorized access. Additionally, inter-state and inter-district borders are sealed well in advance of the election to prevent the movement of illicit materials or disruptive elements across jurisdictional lines. After the polling concludes, Central Armed Police Forces are deployed specifically for guarding strong rooms where electronic voting machines and ballots are stored. The deployment of forces at polling stations follows a strict order of sensitivity, prioritizing Central Armed Police Forces first, followed by State Armed Police, and finally District Armed Police, ensuring that the most trained and neutral forces are present at the most sensitive locations. Additional measures and force multipliers are arranged for critical polling stations to further enhance security, alongside comprehensive logistics arrangements for all security forces.

A crucial aspect of the preparation involves arranging training and briefing sessions for one hundred percent of the personnel involved, leaving no individual unprepared for their duties. Advanced planning includes creating day-to-day schedules for the utilization of central forces for area domination starting from their date of arrival, providing a clear schedule of all areas to be covered to maintain a visible security presence. The complete implementation of district deployment plans is rigorously monitored to ensure ground reality matches the strategic intent. To recapitulate, the process for preparing state level and district level deployment plans consists of a systematic series of steps beginning with an assessment of the local situation and requirements by the district machinery. This is followed by interactions between the office of the Chief Electoral Officer and nodal officers responsible for law and order with the district machinery to accurately assess needs. Data related to criticality and vulnerability, availability of resources, communication shadow areas, regions with historically low voter turnout, areas with low female voter turnout, identified trouble spots, and manpower availability is collected from all districts. This data is then compiled into a comprehensive database at the state level. Based on this database, an indicative deployment plan is prepared at the state level showing the tentative allocation of state police forces. Discussions are then held with the district machinery based on this indicative plan to refine the strategy. The state deployment plan is then firmed up, and an indicative plan for the district level is issued, clearly spelling out the minimum deployment requirements for static duties, mobile patrols, police station reserves, and general reserve forces. Central forces are allocated based on these discussions once their availability is intimated by the Election Commission of India.

The final plan is prepared with specific optimization goals in mind to ensure efficiency and effectiveness. No central force personnel are kept in reserve; instead, every available member is assigned a specific duty to maximize the security footprint. At least eighty percent of the State Police forces are utilized to ensure that local resources are fully leveraged. The maximum number of central forces personnel are deployed for static duties directly at polling stations to deter malpractice and ensure order. Critical polling stations are exclusively covered by central forces to guarantee neutrality and high-level security. Home Guards and related auxiliary forces are utilized specifically for the purpose of maintaining queues at polling stations, managing the flow of voters, while state police personnel are deployed for the broader maintenance of law and order in the surrounding areas. In the District Deployment Plan, it is ensured that all polling stations are covered with adequate static duty forces, which are further reinforced by necessary mobile patrolling organized at the level of zones and sectors to provide rapid response capabilities. Particular attention is paid to deploying Central Armed Police Forces in constituencies that are sensitive regarding expenditure violations and those that are sensitive regarding law and order issues.
