Similarly, instructions have been issued to grant ex-gratia compensation, which is a payment made as a gesture of goodwill rather than legal obligation, to polling and security personnel deployed on election duty in case of any eventuality such as injury or death. This directive must be strictly adhered to ensure prompt payment of compensation to CAPF personnel when needed. Chief Electoral Officers are tasked with planning or establishing tie-ups for cashless medical treatment facilities in coordination with State or Union Territory Health Departments, ensuring access to state-of-the-art hospitals for all deployed personnel, including CAPF, who suffer injuries or fall ill while performing their duties.

Strict protocols must be followed in the unfortunate event of injury or death involving personnel deployed on election duty, including members of the CAPF. In the case of any violent incident or attack, the District Election Officer and the Superintendent of Police must take all necessary measures to ensure the injured receive proper and immediate medical treatment. Additionally, a senior official must be deputed to personally meet with the injured party to offer support. The family of the injured person must be informed immediately, and arrangements should be made to ensure proper coordination and communication with them throughout the recovery process. In the tragic event of a violent attack or a serious accident resulting in the death of any personnel deployed on election duty, the District Election Officer or other senior officials of the district are required to visit the family of the deceased, provided they reside locally, to offer commiserations and condolences. It is imperative that all subsequent formalities, such as the post-mortem examination and the shifting of the dead body, are handled with utmost sensitivity, respect, and without any unnecessary delay, honoring the sacrifice of the personnel who lost their lives in the line of duty while serving the democratic process.

When a tragic incident results in the death of an individual during the election process, and that deceased person hails from a different district within the same state or union territory, or indeed from an entirely different state or union territory, strict protocols must be followed to ensure dignity and timely communication. It is imperative that the details of the incident are conveyed to the family members of the deceased without any delay. This immediate notification is crucial for allowing the family to begin their grieving process and make necessary arrangements. Furthermore, the logistical challenge of transporting the mortal remains back to the native place of the deceased must be handled with great care and coordination. Authorities are responsible for facilitating proper transportation to ensure the body reaches its destination respectfully and safely. The Chief Electoral Officer of the state or union territory where the polling took place and where the incident occurred bears the responsibility of formally informing the Chief Electoral Officer of the state or union territory to which the deceased person belongs. This communication must include comprehensive details such as the full address and other relevant identification information to streamline the process. Upon receiving this information, the concerned Chief Electoral Officer must ensure that a senior officer from the district administration personally meets with the family members of the deceased. This meeting serves multiple critical functions: it is an opportunity to convey the formal commiserations and condolences of the Election Commission, demonstrating institutional empathy, and it is the primary mechanism for coordinating the complex issues surrounding the payment of ex-gratia compensation. Ex-gratia compensation refers to financial assistance granted as a gesture of goodwill rather than due to a legal obligation, and ensuring its swift processing is vital for supporting the bereaved family during a difficult time.

The role of the state police in maintaining the integrity of the electoral process is foundational and extends across various dimensions of security and order. The local state police force retains the primary responsibility for maintaining general law and order throughout the entire area associated with a polling station. This jurisdiction encompasses not only the interior of the polling station premises but also the immediate exterior surroundings, distinguishing between the specific polling booth and the broader designated area. To proactively manage security risks, authorities must identify hamlets, habitations, or specific pockets within the areas concerning polling stations that are vulnerable to threats, intimidation, or undue influence. Undue influence refers to any coercion or pressure exerted on voters to vote in a particular way or abstain from voting, which undermines the freedom of choice. Once these vulnerable areas are identified, all necessary confidence-building measures and preventive actions must be implemented well in advance of the polling day. These measures might include increased patrolling, community engagement, or the establishment of help desks to reassure residents. The local state police must guarantee that there are no hindrances preventing voters in these sensitive pockets from exercising their franchise, or their right to vote, on the day of the poll. In scenarios where the Central Armed Police Forces, often abbreviated as CAPF, which are deployed by the Ministry of Home Affairs, are insufficient in number to cover all requirements, the local State Armed Police or regular local state police units may be deployed exclusively at polling stations. However, this deployment is not arbitrary; it must strictly adhere to the District Deployment Plan that has been reviewed and approved by the senior General Observer and the Police Observer appointed by the Election Commission. When the local state police force is assigned to static duty, meaning they remain stationed at a fixed location rather than patrolling, their placement must follow a rigorous process of randomization to prevent bias and ensure fairness.

The randomization process for police deployment involves specific guidelines to maintain neutrality and operational efficiency. Police constables and Home Guards, who are auxiliary volunteer forces assisting the police, originating from outside the district where they are being deployed, can be assigned to duties without undergoing the randomization process, as their lack of local ties inherently reduces the risk of local bias. Conversely, for constables and Home Guards belonging to the same district, strict matching procedures are required. The lists of these personnel should preferably be cross-referenced with a computerized database maintained by the Home Department, such as a Human Resource Management System or HRMS, to ensure the integrity and accuracy of the deployment lists. In the case of personnel serving within their own district, it is mandatory to ensure that they are deployed only to polling stations that fall outside the geographical jurisdiction of the police station where they are currently posted. This measure prevents conflicts of interest and ensures that officers do not oversee areas where they might have personal connections or prior engagements. Furthermore, wherever practicable, this randomization should be executed in a manner that posts these officers within the same parliamentary constituency where they are themselves enrolled as voters. This strategic placement allows them to exercise their own democratic right to vote through the Electronically Transmitted Postal Ballot System or EDC mechanisms, ensuring that their duty does not disenfranchise them.

Effective coordination between the police and various government agencies and functionaries is absolutely essential for the conduct of elections that are free from incidents and errors. The essence of a successful election lies in collaborative efforts and constructive coordination among diverse entities, which plays a crucial role in upholding the democratic process and ensuring a secure, smooth operation. The Director General of Police holds a pivotal role in orchestrating this coordination with other high-level agencies. Specifically, the coordination with the Chief Secretary or Home Secretary involves several high-stakes responsibilities. The Director General of Police must facilitate the issuance of necessary notifications for the appointment of Special Police Nodal Officers, known as SPNOs, following the approval of the Election Commission of India. This includes overseeing the appointment of a State CAPF coordinator and an Additional Director General or Inspector General of Communications who serves as the Nodal Officer for communication matters, as well as a Nodal Officer dedicated to monitoring election expenditure. These interactions are not merely formalities but involve substantive discussions regarding the status of security forces, the overall law and order scenario within the state, and specific measures required to improve security conditions. The police leadership must provide accurate data related to the availability of the state police force and calculate the requirement for additional forces from other states to meet any shortfall identified for the election period.

Beyond personnel management, the Director General of Police is responsible for logistical and strategic support across state lines. This includes arranging to send additional forces, such as home guards available within the state, to other polling states upon request. They must also provide the approved District Security Deployment Plan and the State Security Deployment Plan, both of which are prepared in strict accordance with the directions issued by the Election Commission. Active participation in review meetings and video conferencing on a regular basis is required to maintain close coordination with the civil administration. The police leadership must bring matters of immediate concern to the table, including issues related to expenditure, procurement of equipment, and the arrangement of air ambulances or helicopters to strengthen police mobility and emergency response capabilities. It is also their duty to raise issues that involve other departments to ensure speedy solutions and proper implementation of plans regarding accommodation for forces, procurement of vehicles, telecommunication equipment, recruitment of drivers, and training programs. The Director General of Police must furnish proposals for the appointment of specific police officers as directed by the Election Commission and handle all related formalities. This extends to obtaining proposals for conferring Executive Magistrate powers on other officers, a legal authority that allows certain officials to maintain public order, and ensuring these powers are officially conferred. Additionally, they are responsible for issuing notifications under Section 28A of the Representation of the People Act, 1951, which governs the deputation of police officers to the Election Commission.

The scope of coordination also covers the mobilization of forces across state boundaries and financial planning. The Director General of Police must ensure the movement and mobilization of State Armed Police Forces for deployment in other states as per directions received from the Ministry of Home Affairs. Financial stewardship is another critical component, involving budget planning for the requirements of both the state police and the Central Armed Police Forces, and ensuring the timely disbursement of funds to the district levels to avoid operational delays. Collaboration on risk assessments and threat analysis is vital to identify vulnerable areas and anticipate potential security challenges before they materialize. The police must coordinate closely to secure the necessary funds and resources for police deployment throughout the election period. This involves regularly updating the Chief Secretary and Home Secretary on evolving resource needs based on the changing security situation, thereby ensuring that timely and adequate provisions are made to support the forces on the ground. Through this intricate web of communication, planning, and execution, the administrative machinery works to safeguard the sanctity of the electoral process, ensuring that every citizen can vote freely and safely while maintaining the highest standards of law and order.

The comprehensive framework for ensuring secure and orderly elections involves a multi-layered approach to coordination between the Director General of Police of a given state and their counterparts in neighboring states. This critical inter-state collaboration necessitates holding regular high-level talks to address shared security challenges that transcend political boundaries. The primary objective of these discussions is to facilitate seamless inter-state coordination, which includes the strategic sealing of borders to prevent the unauthorized movement of individuals or contraband that could disrupt the electoral process. A key component of this strategy involves the establishment and management of interstate nakas, which are temporary checkpoints set up on roads connecting different states to monitor traffic and verify identities. These measures are specifically designed to take decisive action against offenders, habitual criminals, and members of the liquor mafia who often attempt to take shelter in neighboring jurisdictions to evade local law enforcement. By closing these loopholes through joint operations, authorities ensure that no safe haven exists for those seeking to undermine election integrity through violence or illicit trade.

Parallel to border management, extensive coordination is required with the Department of Railways to guarantee enhanced security measures at major railway hubs and throughout the transit network. This partnership is vital for preventing any tampering with or unauthorized access to sensitive election materials, such as ballot papers, electronic voting machines, and official documents, while they are being transported across the country. Furthermore, this collaboration ensures the secure and timely transportation of troops from one location to another, which is essential for deploying sufficient security personnel to volatile areas. The loading and unloading of election-related cargo from trains must strictly adhere to established protocols and undergo rigorous security checks to mitigate risks of sabotage or theft. Every step of the logistical chain involving rail transport is monitored to maintain the sanctity of the election material and the safety of the forces moving them.

The interaction with the Chief Electoral Officer forms the administrative backbone of election security planning. This relationship begins with a thorough assessment of the availability and requirement of police forces needed to cover all polling stations and sensitive zones. Based on this assessment, a formal demand is sent to the Chief Electoral Officer through the State Police Nodal Officer to request the necessary deployment. Legal compliance is maintained by providing a copy of the notification issued under Section 28A of the Representation of the People Act, 1951, which legally authorizes the deputation of police officers to the Election Commission of India for election duties. The police apparatus is also responsible for providing various reports and intelligence inputs sought by the Election Commission during their visits and in the preparation phases. Additionally, the police must submit detailed enquiry reports regarding any security matters or complaints that arise, ensuring transparency and accountability. It is imperative to ensure the full implementation of all directions received from the Election Commission via the Chief Electoral Officer. This coordination extends to logistical support, including sending requisitions for specialized transport assets such as helicopters, air ambulances, and water transport vehicles to handle emergencies and access remote terrains.

The role of the State Police Nodal Officer is central to orchestrating these complex operations. One of their primary tasks is to assess data related to a multilateral augmentation plan, which involves arranging for police forces and home guards from neighboring states or union territories on mutually acceptable terms. This mechanism is crucial for addressing any deficiency in the state's own police force that may result from large-scale retirements or a lack of fresh inductions, ensuring that manpower shortages do not compromise security. Following the announcement of elections, the Nodal Officer conducts a daily review of meetings concerning law and order and other security issues. This involves a continuous review and assessment of the detailed daily law and order situation across the state, ensuring the timely filing of specific documentation known as LOR-I and LOR-II, which are standardized reports on the law and order status. The officer must also attend review meetings with the Election Commission to present ground realities. They are tasked with sending existing local force data for each district along with requirements for additional forces or home guards from outside states if gaps are identified. Furthermore, they must furnish the specific requirements for Central Armed Police Forces during the election period and provide data regarding Critical Polling Stations, which are identified based on parameters set by the Election Commission due to their history of sensitivity or vulnerability. The Nodal Officer works closely with the District Election Officer to prepare comprehensive State and District Deployment Plans that account for various geographical and demographic factors. They are also responsible for sending reports on preventive actions taken, seizures of illegal cases, and confiscation of liquor. Regular attendance at review meetings allows them to raise matters of mutual concern, particularly regarding border districts and interstate border areas where jurisdiction overlaps. To streamline security efforts, regular coordination meetings involving all concerned agencies are held, and joint security exercises are conducted to enhance interoperability and coordination among different security units, ensuring they can operate as a cohesive force.

At the district level, coordination with the Superintendent of Police or Commissioner of Police is essential for addressing election-related issues specific to local contexts. This involves issuing immediate directions on concerns raised by these senior officers through proper channels or brought to light by other agencies, ensuring timely implementation and actionable responses at the district level. Beyond the police hierarchy, collaboration with other government agencies is indispensable. The Ministry of Home Affairs plays a pivotal role by facilitating the acquisition of helicopters for deployment in naxal-affected areas and other inaccessible regions. This ministry also serves as a hub for receiving intelligence inputs, coordinating the movement of Central Armed Police Forces and State Armed Police with the State Force Coordinator, and procuring sensitive communication equipment, arms, and ammunition required for high-risk operations. The Ministry of Railways is engaged specifically for the movement of Central Armed Police Forces by rail from other states, ensuring that troop mobilization is efficient and secure. The State Department of Transportation is tasked with carrying out the requisition of various vehicles, including trucks, buses, and light motor vehicles, along with skilled drivers, to ensure the hassle-free movement of security forces within the state.

Central and State Enforcement Agencies, including the Income Tax Department, Central GST Department, State Excise Department, Narcotics Control Bureau, Enforcement Directorate, Railway Protection Force, Central Industrial Security Force, and Border Security Force, are coordinated with to curb the menace of money and muscle power in elections. This multi-agency effort focuses on the seizure of contraband items, illicit liquor, freebies distributed to influence voters, and illegal arms and ammunition. The sharing of relevant information and the provision of assistance in a timely manner among these agencies are critical for dismantling networks that attempt to manipulate election outcomes through financial inducements or coercion. The Department of Health contributes by arranging cashless treatment for security personnel and polling parties, ensuring their well-being during strenuous duties. This involves timely agreements with state-of-the-art hospitals, procurement of necessary medicines for police personnel, ensuring the availability of paramedic staff at police headquarters, and the preparation of comprehensive medical kits. The department also ensures the availability of air ambulances for the timely evacuation of injured personnel in emergency situations.

The Department of Communication supports the operation by facilitating the procurement of Wi-Fi systems, wireless networks, and Very High Frequency radio sets to maintain robust communication lines. Beyond hardware, this department helps devise engagement strategies that involve the police in educating the public about their role in maintaining a safe election environment. Together, they work on outreach programs designed to build trust and understanding between the police force and local communities, fostering a cooperative atmosphere. Protocols for crisis communication are established in collaboration with the police to ensure accurate and timely dissemination of information during emergencies, thereby maintaining public safety and trust. By focusing on these police-centric strategies and collaborations with various agencies, the police can play a critical role in ensuring the security and smooth conduct of elections in India. Intelligence agencies, specifically the Intelligence Bureau and the State Intelligence Bureau, collaborate closely on intelligence gathering and analysis to proactively identify security threats and challenges during the election period, allowing for preemptive action against potential disruptions. Finally, the National Cyber Security Agency collaborates to enhance cyber security protocols, safeguarding election databases, infrastructure, and communication systems against sophisticated cyber threats. Joint training programs are conducted to enhance the cyber resilience of both the police force and electoral systems, ensuring that digital vulnerabilities do not become entry points for malicious actors seeking to compromise the democratic process.

The District Prosecution Office, also known as the Prosecution Department, plays a critical and multifaceted role in ensuring the integrity of the electoral process by focusing on the swift and timely resolution of legal matters that could otherwise disrupt or undermine elections. This office is specifically tasked with coordinating efforts to dispose of pending cases related to previous elections, ensuring that past grievances or unresolved legal issues do not carry over and negatively impact current polling activities. Furthermore, the department prioritizes cases of a serious nature that possess the potential to have significant repercussions on the electoral process, such as those involving voter intimidation, ballot tampering, or widespread fraud. By accelerating the judicial handling of these sensitive matters, the prosecution office helps maintain public confidence in the fairness of the election and ensures that justice is administered without unnecessary delay, thereby preventing the weaponization of legal delays for political gain.

The Civil Aviation Authority serves as a vital partner in securing the three-dimensional space above the nation during election periods, undertaking complex responsibilities to regulate and protect airspace. This coordination is particularly crucial concerning the movement of Very Important Persons, or VIPs, whose safe transit is essential for campaign activities and official duties, as well as the secure airdrop of election materials to remote or inaccessible regions where ground transportation may be impractical or unsafe. The authority facilitates the rapid movement and emergency evacuation of security forces and essential resources using helicopters, ensuring that logistical bottlenecks do not hinder operational readiness. Additionally, the operation of medical air ambulances is coordinated to provide immediate life-saving support in case of emergencies arising during the high-stress environment of an election. A key component of their mandate involves developing comprehensive plans to restrict the usage of unauthorized drones during the electoral period. This measure is designed to maintain both security and privacy, preventing aerial surveillance by bad actors, the dropping of illicit materials, or any disruption to the voting process through unmanned aerial vehicles that could compromise the sanctity of the poll.

State Fire Services collaborate extensively with election authorities to guarantee fire safety at all election venues, including polling stations, counting centers, and storage facilities where sensitive electronic voting machines and paper ballots are kept. This collaboration involves conducting joint inspections to identify potential fire hazards, ensuring that extinguishing equipment is functional, and verifying that evacuation routes are clear and accessible. Beyond inspection, the fire services provide specialized fire safety training to election staff and volunteers, empowering them to handle initial fire incidents effectively before professional help arrives. To further enhance preparedness, the department develops detailed contingency plans tailored to various scenarios and conducts regular mock drills. These simulations allow all stakeholders to practice their roles in a controlled environment, ensuring that in the event of a real fire emergency, the response is swift, organized, and effective, thereby minimizing risk to human life and protecting critical electoral infrastructure from damage.

The National Disaster Response Force Authority and the State Disaster Response Force Authority work in close coordination with the National Disaster Management Authority to develop and implement robust disaster response and management plans specifically calibrated for the election period. These plans take into account the possibility of natural calamities such as floods, earthquakes, cyclones, or severe storms that might occur during voting or counting days and could severely affect the electoral process. The objective is to ensure that even in the face of adverse natural events, the election can proceed safely or be paused and resumed without compromising the validity of the votes cast. To achieve this, these forces conduct joint training sessions and preparedness exercises with local administration and police forces. These exercises enhance the overall disaster response capabilities of the region, ensuring that personnel are well-versed in rescue operations, crowd management during crises, and the protection of electoral materials, ultimately safeguarding the democratic process against acts of nature.

The State Excise Department collaborates with election officials to strictly monitor and regulate the sale and distribution of alcohol throughout the election period. This regulatory oversight is essential to prevent the misuse of alcohol as a tool for influencing voters, a practice often referred to as liquor bribery, where substances are distributed to impair judgment or induce voters to support specific candidates. The department coordinates closely with law enforcement to enforce strict adherence to election-related prohibitions, which often include dry days where the sale of alcohol is completely banned in certain areas or across the entire state. By controlling the supply chain and cracking down on illegal distillation and smuggling, the Excise Department helps create an environment where voters can make free and informed choices without being subjected to coercion or inducement through intoxicants.

The role of the State Police Nodal Officer is central to the administrative machinery required for conducting free and fair elections, acting as a primary liaison to raise and resolve issues that involve multiple government departments. This officer is responsible for identifying bottlenecks in areas such as accommodation for deployed forces, procurement of essential supplies, allocation of vehicles, provision of telecommunication equipment, recruitment of drivers, and organization of training programs, ensuring speedy solutions for proper implementation. A critical function of this role is to furnish detailed budget proposals for the conduct of the election and to actively pursue these matters with the Home Department to ensure timely allocation of funds, preventing financial delays from hampering operations. Furthermore, the State Police Nodal Officer maintains coordination with neighboring State Police Nodal Officers to synergize efforts in curbing money power and muscle power, which are persistent threats to electoral integrity. This cross-border cooperation involves the sharing of intelligence inputs regarding criminal networks, suspicious financial transactions, and potential troublemakers, allowing for a unified regional approach to suppressing illegal activities.

Central and State Enforcement Agencies play a pivotal role in supporting the election machinery by maintaining constant communication and operational coordination. Agencies such as the Income Tax Department, Central Goods and Services Tax Department, State Excise Department, Narcotics Control Bureau, Enforcement Directorate, Railway Protection Force, Central Industrial Security Force, and Border Security Force are engaged to curb the menace of money and muscle power. Their collaborative efforts focus on the seizure of contraband items, including illegal liquor, unauthorized freebies intended to bribe voters, and unlicensed arms and ammunition. By sharing relevant information and providing manpower and material resources in a timely manner, these agencies create a multi-layered security net that deters criminal elements from attempting to disrupt the election. The presence and active participation of these diverse enforcement bodies signal a zero-tolerance policy towards electoral malpractices and ensure that the playing field remains level for all participants.

The Commissioner of Police or Superintendent of Police holds a position of immense responsibility, requiring seamless coordination with the District Election Officer for all election-related activities and the preparation of a comprehensive District security plan. This plan serves as the blueprint for maintaining law and order throughout the constituency. The police chief must also coordinate with inter-border and intra-border district Superintendents of Police to address election-related matters that transcend jurisdictional lines, ensuring swift actions against mafia groups, executing seizures of illegal assets, and apprehending offenders. Regular contact with counterparts in adjacent districts is maintained to ensure continuity of surveillance and rapid response capabilities. Additionally, coordination with the department of transportation is essential to plan and secure transportation routes for the movement of election materials. This involves minimizing the risk of tampering or theft during transit, ensuring the timely deployment of police personnel alongside election materials and officials, and establishing protocols to respond swiftly to emergencies such as ambushes or accidents during transportation. The police leadership must also stay in touch with Nodal Officers of various Enforcement Agencies to act in close coordination against the dual threats of financial corruption and physical intimidation.

The role of the Director General of Police or Commissioner of Police of a neighboring state or union territory is equally critical in ensuring the smooth conduct of polls in the state going to elections. This senior officer must ensure proper coordination with their counterpart in the poll-going state and participate regularly in review meetings and video conferencing to align strategies and address emerging challenges. Preventive actions are paramount, including the execution of Non-Bailable Warrants against declared offenders, the deposition of arms by potential troublemakers, and other restrictive measures in the bordering districts of the neighboring state from the day the elections are announced. These steps are taken to ensure that the poll-going state enjoys a free, fair, and peaceful election environment without interference from across the border. Sharing intelligence on criminals and anti-social elements with the poll-going state allows for preemptive action against those who might attempt to disrupt the peace. Strict action is taken against absconders, history sheeters, and individuals involved in past electoral offenses to neutralize threats before they materialize.

Furthermore, the neighboring state's police leadership is responsible for providing additional forces, such as home guards, if requested by the poll-going state, subject to availability. They must also ensure necessary facilitation and logistical support, including transport and boarding, for Central Armed Police Forces that are en route to the poll-going states, ensuring these reinforcements arrive fresh and ready for duty. The setting up of integrated check posts at strategic locations in border areas is executed in close coordination with the poll-going state to monitor and control movement. A crucial aspect of this role involves the sealing of entry points and porous inter-state border areas, particularly in the last forty-eight hours before the closing of the poll, to prevent any possibility of bogus voting and the entry of anti-social elements. Vigilance is maintained at the borders to prevent the movement of illicit liquor, narcotics, freebies, and other inducements into the poll-going state. Enhanced surveillance operations are conducted in border areas to carry out seizures of illegal liquor, drugs, cash, freebies, and precious metals, ensuring an inducement-free election. The overarching goal is to maintain a peaceful law and order situation in the bordering areas and districts of the poll-going state. To support these efforts, the declaration of Dry Days, where alcohol sales are prohibited, and Paid Holidays in areas along the border districts helps reduce public unrest and frees up resources for security duties. Finally, a Nodal Officer is appointed in the Director General of Police's office specifically for coordination with the poll-going state, ensuring a dedicated channel of communication. Similarly, the Commissioner of Police or Superintendent of Police of the neighboring state ensures direct coordination with their counterparts in the bordering districts of the poll-going state on all election-related matters, creating a seamless web of security cooperation that transcends administrative boundaries to protect the democratic process.

The maintenance of international, intra-state, and inter-state borders during election periods represents a critical component of ensuring free and fair democratic processes in India. This comprehensive framework is grounded in the specific instructions and guidelines issued by the Election Commission of India, which are formally documented in a specialized publication known as the Manual on Force Deployment in Elections. This manual serves as the authoritative guide for security agencies and administrative bodies, outlining the precise protocols necessary to secure the nation's territorial boundaries against illicit activities that could compromise electoral integrity. The primary objective of these measures is to prevent the infiltration of anti-social elements, the smuggling of prohibited goods such as liquor and illegal firearms, and the movement of individuals with criminal histories who might seek to influence election outcomes through coercion or violence. The scope of this security apparatus extends across three distinct types of boundaries: the international borders that separate India from neighboring countries, the internal borders between different states within the union, and the coastal frontiers along the Arabian Sea, the Bay of Bengal, and the Indian Ocean. Each of these frontier types requires tailored strategies while adhering to a unified command structure designed to maximize coordination and effectiveness.

A fundamental mechanism employed to secure these boundaries is the systematic conduct of border meetings between states that share common frontiers. These gatherings are not merely informal discussions but are mandated procedural steps initiated by the State Nodal Officer for Law and Order, a senior official designated to oversee security coordination within a state. These meetings must occur at two distinct administrative levels to ensure both strategic alignment and tactical execution. At the state level, high-ranking officials convene to establish broad policies and resource allocation, while at the district level, field commanders and local administrators meet to address specific geographical challenges and implement ground-level operations. The imperative for complete cooperation among all concerned states is absolute, particularly regarding the sealing of borders prior to the commencement of polling. This sealing process involves the physical and operational closure of unauthorized crossing points and the intensification of surveillance at authorized checkpoints, known locally as nakas. Effective checking at these inter-state nakas is crucial for intercepting antisocial persons, confiscating illicit liquor, and seizing illegal arms before they can enter constituencies where elections are being held. To enhance the efficacy of these operations, commanders of the Central Armed Police Forces, which are federal paramilitary organizations deployed to assist state police, may be directly involved in these inter-agency interactions, bringing additional manpower and expertise to the border security effort.

States are required to go beyond passive monitoring and actively make efforts to neutralize major suppliers of liquor and drugs who target states going to polls. A complex challenge in this domain is the transit nature of certain border states; often, a state sharing a border with an election-going region acts merely as a corridor through which contraband passes, while the actual source of supply may be a distant state that does not share any direct boundary with the election venue. Consequently, security strategies must account for these multi-jurisdictional supply chains, requiring intelligence sharing and coordinated action across a wider geographical network than just the immediate neighbors. Similarly, strict control must be exerted over the manufacturing of illegal arms and their subsequent supply from bordering states into poll-going states. This involves raiding clandestine workshops, tracking the movement of components, and dismantling distribution networks that thrive on the heightened demand for weapons during volatile election periods. If the situation demands, border states are obligated to assist in the arrest of absconders and history sheeters, a term referring to individuals with a recorded history of criminal activity, especially those implicated in election-related offenses in the neighboring poll-going states. This cross-border arrest capability ensures that criminals cannot evade justice simply by stepping across a state line.

To curb the influence of muscle power, which refers to the use of physical force or intimidation by hired thugs to sway voters or disrupt polling, border states must maintain a vigilant watch on the hiring and transportation of men with criminal backgrounds from their territories into election zones. This preventive measure aims to stop the flow of hired muscle before it reaches the destination, thereby reducing the potential for violence on the ground. Furthermore, border states are tasked with assisting in the apprehension of persons wanted for prohibition-related offenses if they have fled into their jurisdiction, ensuring that violations of liquor bans do not go unpunished due to jurisdictional gaps. To handle any eventuality or emergency requirement, border states must ensure the availability of dedicated forces stationed at police stations located directly on the border. This readiness posture allows for immediate response to breaches or incidents without waiting for reinforcements from deeper within the state. Complementing these personnel deployments is the need for strict vigil by the Excise Department in border states, specifically targeting distilleries to prevent the proliferation of illegally produced alcohol into poll-going states. The integration of technology is also emphasized, with the mandatory use of Closed-Circuit Television coverage at checkpoints on both National Highways and State Highways to create a digital record of movement and deter smuggling attempts. Additionally, border states are instructed to establish checkposts that correspond directly to those of the poll-going states at inter-state borders, creating a mirrored surveillance system that leaves no gap unmonitored.

For the purpose of achieving smooth and effective inter-state coordination, a structured hierarchy of meetings and communication channels has been established involving the highest levels of state administration. The Chief Secretary, who is the top bureaucratic head of a state, the Home Secretary, responsible for internal security, and the Director General of Police, the highest-ranking police officer, from bordering states must convene to plan arrangements for the pre-poll, poll-day, and post-poll phases. These high-level summits focus on determining deployment patterns in bordering areas, deciding on preventive actions, addressing common concerns such as the regulation of inter-state movement of liquor and cash, and setting up complementary checkposts on both sides of the border to ensure seamless inspection. Below this apex level, a nodal officer not below the rank of Inspector General of Law and Order from each state is required to maintain daily contact with their counterparts. This continuous communication loop is vital for real-time intelligence sharing and for reviewing the effectiveness of checkpoints, preventive measures, and any law and order incidents of concern. This ensures that emerging threats are identified and addressed immediately rather than through delayed reporting channels.

At the district level, which is the primary unit of field administration, similar coordination meetings must be held involving the Deputy Inspector General of Police, the District Magistrate who serves as the chief executive officer of the district, and the Superintendent of Police who heads the district police force. These officials meet to engage in granular, field-level planning and coordination, translating state-level directives into actionable tasks on the ground. To facilitate this smooth and effective coordination, nodal officers should be appointed by the District Administration of the bordering districts. The Additional District Magistrate, who often doubles as the Nodal Officer for Law and Order, along with the Additional Superintendent of Police, are considered best suited for this role due to their operational authority and familiarity with local conditions. As the election approaches, there is a specific mandate for the strengthening of these nakas during the critical window of the last twenty-four to seventy-two hours before polling begins. During this heightened alert period, several specific assurances must be met to guarantee security. First, it must be ensured that all roads, including link roads and kutcha tracks, which are unpaved rural paths often used to bypass main highways, having inter-state or inter-district links are covered with the deployment of sufficient numbers of security forces. Leaving these minor routes unguarded could render the entire checkpoint system ineffective.

Secondly, all equipment provided at these naka points, ranging from communication devices to vehicle inspection tools and lighting systems, must be verified to be in full working condition to avoid operational failures during critical moments. Thirdly, the police personnel deployed at these locations must be fully aware of the nature of their duty, understanding exactly what they are looking for and how to handle various scenarios ranging from routine checks to hostile confrontations. Intensive checking of vehicles at these naka points should be carried out rigorously during this pre-election period, moving beyond random sampling to comprehensive inspections of cargo and passengers. Any information regarding the movement of criminals, anti-social elements, or anti-national elements must be shared immediately with neighboring states, specifically communicating directly with the Station House Officers of adjacent police stations in those neighboring states to enable rapid interdiction. The state police will also coordinate closely with the Central Armed Police Force units manning the border and various agencies of the central government to create a unified security front. A joint committee comprising officials from the relevant Central Armed Police Force, the Intelligence Bureau which handles domestic intelligence, the Research and Analysis Wing responsible for external intelligence, the National Crime Bureau which maintains criminal databases, and the Directorate of Revenue Intelligence which tackles economic offenses and smuggling at land ports, should be constituted on the very day the election is declared by the Election Commission of India. This multi-agency body ensures that diverse intelligence streams are merged and acted upon collectively. Coordination meetings between the nominees of various stakeholders of this committee should be held on a regular basis throughout the election cycle. This committee will meet regularly to coordinate all issues regarding border management and to tackle other significant challenges such as the smuggling of drugs, arms, ammunition, and explosives, as well as to formulate other security measures to be taken by security agencies in border areas in wake of the elections, thereby creating a robust, multi-layered defense system that protects the sanctity of the electoral process from external and internal threats.

During critical periods such as elections or times of heightened national sensitivity, it is imperative that comprehensive police and security arrangements are meticulously planned and executed to ensure the maintenance of proper law and order within the nation. The primary objective of these measures is to strictly monitor and control the movement of dangerous criminals who may seek to exploit temporary lapses in security, while simultaneously preventing the illegal supply and trafficking of contraband items such as narcotics, illicit liquor, firearms, ammunition, and other prohibited materials. To achieve this level of security, the protective framework along the International border must be significantly strengthened, creating a robust barrier against cross-border threats. This involves treating the International border not merely as a geographical line but as a dynamic zone requiring a Second Line of Defence, which acts as an additional layer of security inland from the actual border fence or zero line. A thorough and comprehensive review of the existing security protocols at both the immediate border and this secondary defence line must be conducted by designated high-level committees working in tandem with officials from the local District Administration. These reviews are essential to identify gaps in the current system and to formulate actionable strategies for improvement.

To facilitate seamless coordination and real-time decision-making, a Joint Control Room must be established, serving as the nerve center for security operations. This facility will be jointly manned by officials representing both State police forces and various Central agencies, ensuring that jurisdictional boundaries do not hinder operational effectiveness. The establishment of this control room is time-sensitive and must coincide exactly with the day the Election Commission of India officially declares the election schedule, marking the commencement of the model code of conduct and heightened security protocols. Depending on the extensive length of the International border and the specific geographic challenges of different sectors, it may be necessary to establish multiple such control rooms to ensure adequate coverage and rapid response capabilities across all regions. It is mandatory that these control rooms operate around the clock, with continuous staffing ensured by police officers holding at least the rank of Inspector. This constant vigilance is crucial so that any intelligence or information regarding suspicious cross-border movements can be instantly shared with all relevant stakeholders, allowing for immediate interdiction and coordinated action before threats can materialize within the country's interior.

As part of the Second Line of Defence strategy, all important and strategic points located on roads leading toward the International border must be carefully identified and mapped. These locations will form the backbone of the secondary security setup, acting as filtration points for traffic and individuals moving toward the border zones. At these identified strategic points, effective joint checkpoints, locally known as nakas, should be deployed. These nakas must comprise a mixed team of personnel from the concerned Central Armed Police Force and the local district police, fostering a collaborative approach to security enforcement. It is vital that a sufficient number of police personnel are stationed at these Second Line of Defence nakas to handle high volumes of traffic and potential confrontations. Furthermore, the deployment of special vehicles, specifically those that are bullet-resistant, is required at these checkpoints to ensure the safety of the security forces in the event of an armed attack or hostile engagement. To maintain operational cohesion, effective wireless communication systems must be planned and implemented for all such nakas, ensuring that every checkpoint remains in constant contact with the Joint Control Room and neighboring units regardless of terrain or weather conditions. Additionally, the welfare of the security forces, often referred to as jawans, deployed at these remote and demanding posts must be prioritized by ensuring proper accommodation and reliable arrangements for food and refreshments, thereby maintaining their morale and physical readiness for prolonged duties.

In addition to the fixed nakas established along the Second Line of Defence, the security protocol mandates the deployment of surprise nakas during night time in border areas. These unpredictable checkpoints are designed to disrupt the routines of undesirable elements and smugglers who often rely on predictable patrol patterns to evade detection. To further enhance situational awareness, a sophisticated Closed-Circuit Television or CCTV camera surveillance system should be established, featuring a centralized command center located at the district headquarters. This setup allows senior officials to monitor live feeds and coordinate responses from a single location. Vulnerable and strategic points within the border region must be identified through intelligence analysis, and high-quality CCTV cameras should be installed at these specific locations. The technical specifications for these cameras require them to be IP-based infrared models, which provide the capability to capture clear video footage even in complete darkness, thus eliminating blind spots during night operations. Complementing this technological surveillance, Rapid Police Response vehicles and other mobile units should be strategically positioned near the border during night hours to ensure that forces can reach any incident location within minutes.

A mechanism of joint patrolling and checking must be deployed along the International border, involving close cooperation between the local police and the concerned Central Armed Police Force. This collaborative presence serves as a visible deterrent to illegal activities and ensures that both state and central resources are utilized optimally. To sustain this high level of coordination, regular meetings should be held between the local units of the Central Armed Police Force, the local police, and other relevant agencies from both the State and Central governments. These forums are essential for discussing multifarious issues related to border security, sharing ground-level intelligence, and resolving operational friction. Strict surveillance measures must be deployed to cover a depth of at least one thousand meters on the Indian side from the zero line of the border, creating a dense monitoring grid. Within this zone, surprise checkings, ambushes, and intensive patrolling should be organized, particularly during odd hours and throughout the night when criminal activity is most likely to occur under the cover of darkness.

The threat landscape has evolved to include aerial surveillance and smuggling via unmanned aerial vehicles, commonly known as drones or UAVs. Consequently, the Senior Superintendents or Superintendents of Police in border districts are tasked with identifying vulnerable areas within their respective jurisdictions that could serve as launchpads for these drones. Once identified, these locations must be covered with intensified police patrolling to prevent unauthorized launches. Furthermore, regular meetings with the local population should be conducted to educate them about various security threats prevalent in border areas, including the dangers and legal implications of drone operations. The people living in these border regions play a critical role as the eyes and ears of the security apparatus; therefore, they must be sensitized to these issues through well-devised and implemented community outreach programs by the district police. Building trust and awareness among the local community ensures that residents are more likely to report suspicious activities, thereby strengthening the overall security net.

Operational tactics must also include surprise and intensive checking of vehicles in border areas, conducted rigorously during both day and night to detect concealed contraband or wanted individuals. Special combing and search operations should be carried out at places deemed suspicious based on intelligence inputs or historical data. The Senior Superintendents or Superintendents of Police of border districts have the specific responsibility of identifying major smugglers of drugs and weapons operating in their areas, as these criminal elements often facilitate illegal incursions and excursions across the border. Effective and continuous surveillance must be mounted on the activities of these identified kingpins to dismantle their networks and cut off the supply chains of illegal goods. The intelligence sharing mechanism between local units of the State Intelligence wing and the Central Armed Police Force manning the borders must be significantly strengthened to counter any security threat emanating from the territory of neighboring countries. Timely and accurate intelligence is the cornerstone of preventive security, allowing forces to act before a breach occurs.

The speed of police response is a critical factor in the success of these operations. The response time of the police must be immediate and without any delay, as criminals and infiltrators act with great speed and precision. In cases where the police response is delayed, perpetrators are highly likely to escape from the scene of the crime or cross back into foreign territory, rendering the interception futile. Therefore, protocols must ensure that forces are always in a state of high alert and ready to deploy instantly. Suspicious movement of people near the border and in areas extending at least three to four kilometers from the border line should be thoroughly checked, especially during night time by the local police. Specific attention must be paid to identifying and earmarking drone target points, landing areas, and dropping zones used for smuggling payloads from across the border. This measure is particularly relevant and urgent for the border areas of Punjab, Rajasthan, and the Union Territory of Jammu and Kashmir, where such incidents have been historically noted. Finally, a sufficient number of strong and well-manned nakas in each border district should be earmarked specifically for search operations. This selection process should be carried out by the concerned Inspector General of Police or Senior Superintendent of Police in close consultation with authorities from the Central Armed Police Force and other central agencies, ensuring that the chosen locations offer the best tactical advantage for intercepting illegal activities.

In the comprehensive framework of maintaining public order and security during sensitive periods such as elections, specific provisions are made to integrate specialized military expertise into civilian law enforcement coordination. Specifically, members of the Indian Army and the Indian Air Force may be formally included in strategic committees tasked with addressing the emerging threat of illicit drops involving weapons and narcotics delivered via unmanned aerial vehicles, commonly known as drones. This inclusion recognizes the technical proficiency of armed forces personnel in detecting and neutralizing aerial threats that traditional police units might lack the equipment or training to handle effectively. Concurrently, to bolster ground-level security, senior-ranking police officers must be officially nominated to supervise special search operations and night domination patrols. These operations are strategically concentrated near the second line of defence, which serves as a critical buffer zone intended to intercept threats before they penetrate deeper into populated or politically sensitive areas. The concept of night domination refers to proactive policing measures taken after dark to assert control over territory, thereby denying criminals the cover of darkness to move contraband or execute illegal activities.

A central component of this security architecture is the system of Inter-State Nakas, a term derived from local vernacular meaning checkpoints or barricades established at border crossings. The primary and overarching objective of these nakas is to prevent criminal activities and arrest the movement of dangerous individuals, including terrorists, organized gangsters, and smugglers dealing in drugs, liquor, arms, ammunition, explosives, and unaccounted cash. These checkpoints act as filters preventing the flow of such illicit goods and persons from other states into regions where elections are imminent. By rigorously monitoring the flow of traffic between states, law enforcement agencies can effectively address and dismantle smuggling networks that operate across jurisdictional boundaries. The context of elections adds a layer of urgency, as historical data suggests that certain groups often employ illegal services of musclemen, colloquially referred to as goonda elements, to engage in election rigging, voter intimidation, or violence. Frequently, these hired enforcers are brought in from neighboring states to avoid local identification and to terrorize the electorate. Therefore, inter-state and inter-district nakas play an indispensable role in identifying, stopping, and preventing the movement of these undesirable and dangerous elements. However, it is fundamentally important to emphasize that the establishment and operation of these checkpoints must strictly adhere to the legal framework of the nation. Law enforcement agencies are mandated to respect individual rights and follow constitutional principles, specifically the requirements of probable cause and reasonable suspicion, when conducting searches and seizures. Probable cause refers to the standard of proof requiring sufficient reason based on known facts to believe a crime has been committed, while reasonable suspicion is a lower standard allowing officers to briefly detain individuals if specific and articulable facts suggest criminal activity. These safeguards ensure that while security is tightened, civil liberties are not compromised. The nakas serve as a visible deterrent to criminal intent and contribute significantly to the overall safety and well-being of the public by ensuring compliance with state laws.

To achieve these security objectives with precision, meticulous compliance with a set of operational guidelines is required at every naka. Interstate nakas, functioning as formal border checkpoints, should be jointly established by the state police forces of both adjoining states at their shared borders. This joint responsibility ensures that there are no gaps in surveillance or enforcement due to jurisdictional ambiguities. These checkpoints are designed to serve multiple purposes, including verifying compliance with varying state laws regarding the transport of goods, preventing the movement of illegal items, and enhancing general public safety. A thorough checking regime must be implemented for all vehicles passing through, which includes the verification of essential documents such as driver's licenses, vehicle registration certificates, and necessary transport permits. Furthermore, vehicles may be subjected to physical searches for contraband items like narcotics, unauthorized weapons, illicit liquor, and explosives. Individuals found to have outstanding arrest warrants may be apprehended directly at these points. To modernize these operations and ensure accountability, state-of-the-art closed-circuit television, or CCTV, surveillance systems must be installed at every naka. These cameras provide real-time monitoring, record evidence of interactions, and act as a check against potential misconduct by personnel. The operational timeline for these nakas is synchronized with the electoral calendar; they must be established from the exact day the Model Code of Conduct comes into force in the concerned state. The Model Code of Conduct is a set of guidelines issued by the Election Commission to regulate the behavior of political parties and candidates during elections, and its implementation marks the beginning of the heightened security phase. These checkpoints must operate round the clock, divided into three distinct shifts to ensure twenty-four-hour coverage without fatigue-induced lapses in vigilance. Regarding manpower deployment, each shift at every inter-state naka must consist of one non-gazetted rank police officer or a head constable, accompanied by three constables of the state police. A non-gazetted officer is a supervisory role below the level of gazetted officers who hold higher executive powers, ensuring that there is always a responsible supervisor present on the ground.

Recognizing the complexity of border management, states have evolved various coordination mechanisms at the state, district, subdivision, and police station levels, particularly for districts sharing an inter-state border. To formalize and streamline these efforts, specific committees are to be constituted immediately upon the announcement of elections. At the State Level, a high-powered committee is formed to oversee the broader strategy. The composition of this committee includes the overall in-charge of the law and order setup of the state, typically an Additional Director General of Police or an Inspector General of Police, who provides top-level strategic direction. Also included is a representative from the state's intelligence or Criminal Investigation Department, or CID, which brings analytical capabilities and deep background information on criminal networks. The committee further comprises the Range Inspector or Deputy Inspector General of Police responsible for districts having inter-state borders, ensuring regional-specific insights are considered. Crucially, a representative of the Chief Electoral Officer of the state is included to align police actions with electoral requirements, along with a representative of the State Police Nodal Officer for elections, who acts as the primary liaison for election-related security matters. The functions of this State Level Committee are extensive and vital. They are responsible for ensuring seamless coordination between the police forces of neighboring states, fostering a collaborative environment rather than a siloed approach. The committee tasks itself with the identification of potential troublemakers, known criminals, smugglers, and gangsters who might attempt to enter the election-bound state. Once identified, all relevant details about such individuals are collected and shared promptly with neighboring states to create a unified watchlist. This information sharing extends to lists of parole jumpers, bail jumpers, and proclaimed offenders or absconders from both states, ensuring that individuals who have violated legal conditions of their release are tracked. The committee facilitates the sharing of relevant and actionable intelligence regarding the movement of these criminals and smugglers on a real-time basis, allowing for dynamic responses to emerging threats. Additionally, details of stolen vehicles, which are often used in crimes during election times to evade detection, are circulated. The committee also plans and launches coordinated police operations on both sides of the interstate borders and ensures that the laying of nakas is done in a tandem and coordinated manner so that no ingress point into the state remains uncovered or vulnerable.

At the District Level, a parallel committee structure is established to handle tactical implementation on the ground. This committee is headed by the Commissioner of Police, Senior Superintendent of Police, or Superintendent of Police of a district that shares an inter-state border, depending on the administrative designation of the district. It also includes the Deputy Superintendent of Police or Circle Inspector of the subdivision having an inter-state border, as well as the Sub-Divisional Magistrate, who represents the civil administration and ensures that legal procedures are followed. The primary functions of the District Level Committee focus on the practical aspects of checkpoint management. They are responsible for the precise identification of locations for establishing interstate nakas, taking into account geography, traffic patterns, and historical crime data to maximize effectiveness. Following the site selection, the committee oversees the establishment of proper pickets, which can be either temporary structures erected for the election duration or permanent facilities, ensuring that the personnel have adequate shelter and operational infrastructure. Through this multi-tiered approach involving military support, senior police supervision, technologically enhanced checkpoints, and robust committee structures at both state and district levels, the administration aims to create an impregnable security grid. This grid is designed not only to intercept physical contraband and dangerous individuals but also to uphold the sanctity of the democratic process by preventing external interference, voter intimidation, and election-related violence, all while operating within the strict bounds of the law and respecting the fundamental rights of citizens.

The comprehensive security framework for maintaining law and order, particularly during sensitive periods such as elections, relies heavily on the strategic establishment and operation of surveillance and checkpoint systems known locally as nakas. A foundational element of this infrastructure is the installation of advanced Internet Protocol based infrared closed-circuit television surveillance systems. These systems are not standalone units but are intricately connected to a centralized control room, allowing for real-time monitoring and rapid response coordination across vast geographical areas. The use of infrared technology ensures that surveillance remains effective even in low-light or nighttime conditions, providing continuous visual coverage regardless of environmental factors. To support these technological measures, it is imperative to provide sufficient hardware and ancillary equipment at these checkpoint locations. This includes physical barriers such as barricades to control traffic flow, high-intensity lighting systems often referred to as dragon lights to illuminate the area thoroughly, portable torches for close-up inspections, and dedicated chase vehicles capable of pursuing suspects who attempt to flee. Furthermore, the operational efficacy of these sites depends on the availability of video cameras for local recording, computers and laptops for data processing and communication, and robust internet connectivity to ensure seamless information exchange between the field and command centers.

Operational protocols extend beyond static defenses to include dynamic activities such as organizing joint flag marches, which serve as a visible demonstration of police presence and authority, thereby acting as a psychological deterrent to potential offenders. These marches are often complemented by need-based search and combing operations conducted specifically in border areas where jurisdictional lines may otherwise create security gaps. To enhance the detection capabilities at these checkpoints, a sufficient number of specially trained sniffer dogs are deployed. These canines are expertly trained to detect specific scents related to explosives and narcotics, adding a critical layer of sensory inspection that technology alone cannot fully replicate. The success of these operations also hinges on the careful selection of proper manpower, ensuring that only personnel with the appropriate skills, training, and integrity are assigned to these sensitive posts. Regular checking and supervision of these nakas are mandated to maintain high standards of performance and accountability. To oversee these functions, a Police Station Level Committee is constituted, comprising Station House Officers from police stations that manage inter-state nakas. This committee is tasked with a wide range of responsibilities designed to ensure total coverage and operational readiness.

The functions of the Police Station Level Committee include ensuring that all types of thoroughfares, including main roads, link roads, and unpaved tracks known as kutcha paths that connect different states, are covered by the deployment of adequate police forces. This prevents criminals from bypassing main checkpoints by using obscure or rural routes. The committee must ensure that the police force is deployed at these nakas in three distinct shifts to guarantee round-the-clock operations without fatigue compromising effectiveness. It is also their duty to verify that all equipment provided at these locations is in perfect working condition, ranging from communication devices to surveillance cameras. Furthermore, the committee must ensure that every police personnel deployed is fully aware of the nature of their duties, understanding both their legal powers and their specific operational mandates. Active duties include the rigorous checking of vehicles to intercept the movement of criminals, proclaimed offenders, absconders who have fled justice, and parole jumpers who have violated the terms of their release. Combing and search operations near interstate borders must be carried out in a highly coordinated manner with adjacent police stations of neighboring states to prevent jurisdictional loopholes from being exploited.

Coordination is a cornerstone of this security architecture, necessitating the organization of regular meetings between Station House Officers of adjacent districts in neighboring states. These meetings facilitate the timely dissemination of intelligence regarding the known movement of criminals, ensuring that police forces in other states, particularly those in adjacent jurisdictions, are forewarned and prepared. There is a specific protocol for sharing lists of hardened criminals, proclaimed offenders, absconders, parole jumpers, and individuals involved in heinous crimes, a practice that becomes especially critical during election periods when the risk of disruption is elevated. The committee is also responsible for briefing district and state level committees about activities at the interstate borders on a regular basis, creating a feedback loop that informs higher-level strategic planning. Parallel to these inter-state efforts are the Inter District Nakas, which serve a primary objective of preventing criminal activities and arresting the movement of dangerous elements such as terrorists, gangsters, and smugglers of drugs, liquor, arms, ammunition, explosives, and unaccounted cash within the districts of a state where elections are being held. These inter-district checkpoints play a vital role in stopping the flow of undesirable elements within the state boundaries, thereby maintaining internal security and ensuring compliance with state laws.

Inter-district nakas act as a visible deterrent to criminal activities and contribute significantly to the overall safety and well-being of the public. They should be established by the concerned state authorities at the borders of districts to monitor and regulate the movement of both vehicles and individuals. Their purposes are multifaceted, including ensuring adherence to state regulations, preventing the transportation of illegal goods, and enhancing general public safety. The activation of these nakas is timed to coincide with the implementation of the model code of conduct in the state, marking the beginning of the strict regulatory phase leading up to elections. At these locations, the checking of vehicles must be thorough and meticulous. Vehicles are to be searched for contraband items such as drugs, weapons, and illicit liquor, and individuals with outstanding warrants are to be apprehended immediately. Where available, a sufficient number of sniffer dogs should be deployed to assist in these inspections. Modern, state-of-the-art CCTV surveillance systems, specifically IP based infrared models connected to the district control room, must be installed to provide constant oversight. These nakas are required to operate twenty-four hours a day across three shifts, with each shift staffed by one non-gazetted rank police officer or a head constable, along with three constables, ensuring a balanced team structure for effective enforcement.

The Station House Officer of the area bears significant responsibility for the successful execution of these measures. Officers from adjoining districts must coordinate closely to identify the most suitable locations for establishing inter-district nakas, taking into account traffic patterns and historical crime data. Proper pickets, which may be temporary or permanent structures, must be erected at these sites to provide shelter and operational bases for the personnel. It is mandatory to provide sufficient hardware and equipment, including barricades, dragon lights, torches, chase vehicles, video cameras, and computers with internet connectivity, ensuring that the workforce has the necessary tools to perform their duties. The Station House Officer must continually verify that all equipment is functional and that the deployed personnel are fully briefed on their roles. Regular coordination meetings with Station House Officers of adjacent districts are essential to maintain synergy, and the timely sharing of intelligence regarding criminal movements is crucial for proactive policing. This collaborative approach ensures that no district acts in isolation, creating a unified front against cross-district criminal activity.

In addition to border and district security, VIP security constitutes a very important aspect of any election-related planning. During elections, ensuring foolproof security for Very Important Persons, including candidates, political leaders, star campaigners, and other key political functionaries, becomes paramount. This requirement is driven by the heightened risks associated with political rallies and public appearances during campaign periods. The need for stringent security measures becomes even more sensitive and critical in areas affected by extremist activities or regions influenced by Left Wing Extremism. In such volatile environments, security planning requires thorough preparation, detailed logistical planning, continuous monitoring, and effective deployment of resources. The safety of these individuals is not just a matter of personal protection but is integral to the smooth conduct of the democratic process, as any incident involving a high-profile leader could destabilize the election environment and incite unrest. Therefore, the security apparatus must be adaptable, intelligence-driven, and capable of responding swiftly to emerging threats while maintaining a visible yet non-intrusive presence that allows political activities to proceed safely.

The aspect of VIP security must never be neglected during the conduct of elections, as this period presents unique challenges where security forces and various government agencies are primarily engaged in a wide array of election-related activities and extensive preparations. It is critically important that the protection of Very Important Persons, often referred to as VIPs, be treated with the utmost seriousness and handled with the highest degree of professional competence. During election cycles, the movement of political leaders, candidates, and high-ranking officials increases significantly, creating complex security scenarios that require dedicated attention separate from general election duty. To address these needs effectively, a comprehensive framework of measures is suggested to ensure the safety of these individuals without compromising the broader electoral process.

A foundational step in this framework is the establishment of a dedicated VIP Security Monitoring Cell, which needs to be made fully functional at both the state level and the district level. The primary purpose of this cell is to serve as a central hub for coordinating with a diverse range of entities, including various security agencies, intelligence organizations, the offices of Chief Electoral Officers and District Election Officers, Superintendents of Police, political parties, control rooms, and other relevant stakeholders. The ultimate goal of this coordination is to ensure incident-free and foolproof security for all VIPs involved in the electoral process. At the state level, the VIP monitoring cell should be headed by an officer of sufficiently high rank who is nominated directly by the Director General of Police of the state.
